Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Whose Word is Taken in a Mudarabah Dispute on Generality or Restriction?
Commentary on the rule that the mudarib's word is taken regarding scope of mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on whose word is taken when the rabb al-mal and mudarib dispute the scope of mudarabah and identify the exception when both agree the contract was restricted.

Core Idea
In mudarabah, the default is generality — the mudarib's word is taken unless both agree on restriction.

When the owner of capital (rabb al-mal) and the mudarib disagree about whether the mudarabah was general or restricted, who should the qadi believe? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position from al-Bahr al-Raiq, explaining the default principle of generality, the exception for agreed restrictions, and an intra-madhhab difference reported from Hasan ibn Ziyad. By understanding these rules, you will grasp how Hanafi law balances the mudarib's operational freedom with the owner's right to limit his investment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Determine whether the parties disagree on generality vs. restriction, or both agree the contract was specific but differ on the object of restriction. The ruling flips based on this distinction.
If rabb al-mal says 'I restricted you to wheat' and mudarib says 'You said nothing', it is the first scenario. If both say 'You did restrict me' but differ on what, it is the second.
2
Apply the default rule: mudarib's word for generality
Recognize that the mere mention of 'mudarabah' gives the mudarib broad authority. Therefore, his claim of generality is consistent with the apparent import of the contract.
The commentator says: 'a la tara annahu yamliku al-tasarrufa bi-dhikri lafzati al-mudarabah' – do you not see that he possesses the right to act by the mere word mudarabah?
3
Locate the exception: rabb al-mal's word when both agree on restriction
If both parties confirm that the mudarabah was muqayyad (restricted), the generality principle no longer applies. The rabb al-mal's word is taken because authorization comes from him and they have departed from the apparent meaning.
This is based on the principle that when both deviate from the default, the source of authorization (rabb al-mal) controls.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
A narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that Abu Hanifa held the rabb al-mal's word even in the default case. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the mudarib's word, as recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
This shows the importance of distinguishing between authoritative (zahir al-riwayah) and rare (nawadir) transmissions.
5
Distinguish mudarabah from bida'ah
In bida'ah (commission agency), the default is restriction; the agent cannot buy/sell freely without explicit permission. Contrast this with mudarabah where the default is generality.
The passage ends by noting that the mustabdi' (bida'ah agent) cannot even deposit goods or sell what he bought unless specified, unlike the mudarib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي المضاربة للمضارب أي لو اختلف رب المال والمضارب في الإطلاق والتقييد فالقول للمضارب لأن الأصل في المضاربة العموم ألا ترى أنه يملك التصرف بذكر لفظة المضاربة فقامت دلالة الإطلاق بخلاف ما إذا ادعى رب المال المضاربة في نوع والآخر في نوع آخر حيث يكون القول لرب المال لأنه سقط الإطلاق بتصادقهما فنزل إلى الوكالة المحضة، ثم مطلق الأمر بالبيع ينتظمه نقد أو نسيئة إلى أي أجل كان عنده، وعندهما يتقيد بأجل متعارف كما قدمناه وفي مضاربة البزازية نوع في الاختلاف مقتضى المضاربة العموم فالقول لمن يدعيها والتخصيص عارض لا يثبت إلا ببينة وإذا اتفقا أن العقد خاصاً وقع واختلفا فيما خص العقد فيه فالقول لرب المال لاتفاقهما على العدول عن الظاهر والإذن يستفاد من قبله فيعتبر قوله أمرتك بالاتجار في البر وادعى الإطلاق فالقول للمضارب لادعائه عمومه. وعن الحسن عن الإمام أنه لرب المال لأن الإذن يستفاد منه وإن برهنا، فإن نص شهود العامل أنه أعطاه مضاربة في كل تجارة فهي أولى لإثباته الزيادة لفظاً ومعنى، وإن لم ينصوا على هذا الحرف فلرب المال وكذا إذا اختلفا في المنع من السفر لاقتضاء المضاربة إطلاقها على الروايات المشهورة قال المضارب هو في الطعام ورب المال. قال في الكرباس فالقول له. وإن برهنا فللمضارب لأن رب المال لا يحتاج إلى الإثبات والمضارب محتاج إلى إثباته لدفع الضمان والبضاعة كالمضاربة إلا أن نفسه وإن وقتاً فالوقت الأخير أولى ا هـ . عن المضارب يملك البيع والمستبضع لا إلا إذا كان في لفظه ما يعلم أنه قصد الاسترباح أو نص على ذلك؛ كذا في وكالة البزازية والظاهر أنها كالوكالة من حيث إن الأصل فيها التقييد إلا أنه لا يملك الإبضاع والإيداع وبيع ما اشتراه إلا بالتنصيص بخلاف المضارب
His saying: (And in mudarabah, it is for the mudarib) meaning if the owner of capital and the mudarib differ regarding generality and restriction, then the word is of the mudarib because the basis in mudarabah is generality. Do you not see that he possesses the right to act by the mere mention of the word mudarabah, so the indication of generality is established, contrary to when the owner of capital claims mudarabah in one type and the other claims another type, where the word is of the owner of capital because generality is nullified by their mutual agreement, so it descends to pure agency. Then, an absolute command to sell encompasses cash or credit to any term according to him (Abu Hanifa), but according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is restricted to a customary term as we have previously mentioned. And in the Mudarabah of al-Bazzaziyyah, there is a type concerning disagreement: the requirement of mudarabah is generality, so the word is for the one who claims it, and specification is an incidental matter that is only established by evidence. If they agree that the contract was specific and then they differ regarding what the contract was specified for, then the word is of the owner of capital because they agree on departing from the apparent, and authorization is derived from him, so his word is considered. (He says: I ordered you to trade in wheat) and he claims generality, then the word is for the mudarib because he claims its generality. And from al-Hasan from al-Imam that it is for the owner of capital because authorization is derived from him, even if they both provide evidence. If the witnesses of the worker state that he gave him a mudarabah in every trade, then that is more worthy because it proves an increase in wording and meaning. If they do not specify this phrase, then it is for the owner of capital. Similarly, if they differ regarding the prohibition of travel, because mudarabah requires its generality according to the famous narrations. The mudarib says: it is in food, and the owner of capital... He said in al-Karbas: the word is for him. If they both provide evidence, then for the mudarib because the owner of capital does not need to prove, while the mudarib needs to prove to remove liability. And bida'ah is like mudarabah except that its permissibility... and if there is a time, the later time is preferable. End. The mudarib may buy and sell, but the mustabdi' may not, unless his wording indicates that he intended profit or he explicitly stated that; as in Wakalat al-Bazzaziyyah. And the apparent is that it is like agency in that the basis in it is restriction, except that he does not have the right to give bida'ah, deposit, or sell what he bought without explicit stipulation, unlike the mudarib.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn ruling 'وفي المضاربة للمضارب'. The commentator, al-Zayla'i, explains that when the rabb al-mal and the mudarib dispute whether the mudarabah was general or restricted, the mudarib's word is taken because the default in mudarabah is generality (al-isl). The proof is that the mudarib is authorized to act merely by the word 'mudarabah', which implies broad authority. However, if both agree the contract was specific but disagree on the specific item, the rabb al-mal's word prevails because the authorization came from him. The passage then records a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that Abu Hanifa said the rabb al-mal's word is taken because authorization derives from him, and if both bring evidence, the mudarib's witnesses if they state 'in every trade' are preferred. The passage also compares mudarabah with bida'ah, noting that the mudarib can buy and sell freely while the mustabdi' (commission agent) cannot without explicit permission. The commentary clarifies that the apparent (zahir) in bida'ah is restriction, unlike mudarabah.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudarabah): A partnership contract where one party provides capital and the other provides labor.
إطلاق (itlaq): Generality or absoluteness in the scope of the mudarabah.
تقييد (taqyid): Restriction or specification of the mudarabah to a particular type or time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if the rabb al-mal claims the mudarabah was restricted to wheat and the mudarib claims it was unrestricted, whose word is accepted?
A) The rabb al-mal's word because he gave authorization.
B) The mudarib's word because the default in mudarabah is generality.
C) Both words are equally considered and the qadi decides based on evidence.
D) The mudarib's word because he is the one acting, but only if he has witnesses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the default in mudarabah is generality; the mudarib's word on scope is accepted unless the contract is proven to be restricted.

Definition and Legal Status of Mudarabah
Definition and legal statuses of mudarib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of mudarabah and identify the five legal statuses of the mudarib.

Core Idea
The mudarib is a trustee, agent, partner, hired worker in corruption, and usurper in violation.

This lesson opens the chapter on mudarabah with a precise definition. It explains the multi-faceted legal personality of the mudarib — his status changes with circumstances, affecting liability and rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the first sentence: mudarabah is a company (sharika) with capital from one side and work from the other. Note that the profit is shared.
2
List the five statuses of the mudarib
The text gives five roles: trustee (amin), agent (wakil), partner (sharik) in profit, hired worker (ajir) if the contract is corrupt, and usurper (ghasib) if he violates terms. Understand the legal consequence of each.
3
Understand stipulation of all profit
If all profit is for one party, it is not mudarabah. That arrangement becomes a loan (qard). Recognize the boundary between mudarabah and loan.
4
Analyze the pillar (rukn)
The pillar is the verbal expression (lafz) indicating mudarabah. Although not in this passage segment, note that rukn is essential for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة هي شركة بمال من جانب وعمل من جانب والمضارب أمين وبالتصرف وكيل وبالربح شريك وبالفساد أجير وبالخلاف غاصب وباشتراط كل الربح له مستقرض كتاب المضاربة (هي شركة في الربح بمال من جانب وعمل من جانب فلو شرط كل الربح لأحدهما لا يكون مضاربة. ويجوز التفاوت في الربح وإذا كان المال من اثنين فلا بد من تساويهما فيما فضل من الربح حتى لو شرط لأحدهما الثلثان وللآخر الثلث فيما فضل فهو بينهما نصفين لاستوائهما في رأس المال وركنها اللفظ الدال عليها كقوله دفعت إليك هذا المال مضاربة أو مفاوضة أو معاملة أو خذ هذا المال واعمل به على أن لك من الربح نصفه أو ثلثه، أو قال ابتع به متاعاً فما كان من فضل فلك كذا، أو خذ ذلك بالنصف بخلاف خذ هذه الألف واشتر بها هروياً بالنصف ولم يزد عليه فليس بمضاربة بل إجارة فاسدة له أجر مثله إن اشترى وليس له البيع إلا بأمر . وشرطها أن يكون رأس المال الأثمان من وهو معلوم ويكفي الإعلام بالإشارة، فإن اختلفا في مقدار رأس المال عند قسمة الربح فالقول للمضارب مع يمينه والبينة لرب المال . وأما المضاربة بدين فإن كان على المضارب فلا يصح وما اشتراه له والدين في ذمته، وإن كان على غيره بأن قال اقبض مالي على فلان ثم اعمل به مضاربة فهو جائز وإن كان مكروهاً لأنه شرط لنفسه منفعة قبل العقد كما في المبسوط . ولو قال اقبض ديني على فلان ثم اعمل به مضاربة فعمل قبل أن يقبض كله ،ضمن ولو قال فاعمل به لا يضمن . وكذا بالواو لأن ثم للترتيب فلا يكون مأذوناً بالعمل إلا بعد قبض الكل بخلاف الفاء والواو فإنه يكفي قبل القبض ولو قال اقبض ديني لتعمل به مضاربة لا يكون مأذوناً ما لم يقبض الكل. ولو قال اشتر لي عبداً بنسيئة ثم بعه واعمل بثمنه مضاربة فاشتراه ثم باعه وعمل فيه جاز. ولو قال رب المال للغاصب أو المستودع أو المبضع اعمل بما في يدك
Book of Mudarabah: It is a company with capital from one side and work from the other. The mudarib is a trustee, and regarding disposition he is an agent, and in profit he is a partner, and in case of corruption he is a hired worker, and in case of violation he is a usurper, and if all profit is stipulated for him, he is a borrower. Book of Mudarabah (It is a partnership in profit with capital from one side and work from the other. If all profit is stipulated for one of them, it is not mudarabah. Disparity in profit is permissible. If the capital is from two, then they must be equal in the surplus profit; so if one stipulates two-thirds and the other one-third of the surplus, it is half and half because they are equal in capital. Its pillar is the expression indicating it, like saying: I gave you this capital as mudarabah, or mufawada, or mu'amala, or take this capital and work with it on condition that you have half or one-third of the profit, or he said: buy goods with it, and whatever profit there is, you have such-and-such, or take that for half. Unlike: take these thousand and buy with them Herawi cloth for half, and did not add more; that is not mudarabah but a void contract of hire, and he is entitled to his equivalent wage if he buys, and he has no right to sell except by order. Its condition is that the capital be from coins (thaman) and it be known, and it is sufficient to indicate it by pointing. If they differ in the amount of capital at the time of dividing profit, the word is of the mudarib with his oath, and the evidence is for the owner of capital. As for mudarabah with a debt: if it is on the mudarib, it is not valid, and whatever he buys is for him and the debt remains in his liability. If it is on someone else, such as he said: collect my money from so-and-so then work with it as mudarabah, it is permissible although disliked because he stipulated a benefit for himself before the contract, as in al-Mabsut. If he said: collect my debt from so-and-so then work with it as mudarabah, and he worked before collecting all of it, he guarantees. If he said: 'fa'lam bihi' (then work with it) he does not guarantee. Likewise with 'waw' because 'thumma' implies sequence, so he is not permitted to work except after collecting all; contrary to 'fa' and 'waw', they suffice before collection. If he said: collect my debt to work with it as mudarabah, he is not permitted until he collects all. If he said: buy for me a slave on credit, then sell him and work with his price as mudarabah, and he bought, then sold, and worked with it, it is permissible. If the owner of capital said to a usurper, a depositary, or a bailee: work with what is in your hand...
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the Book of Mudarabah, providing a comprehensive definition and many rulings. Mudarabah is defined as a company (sharika) in profit: capital from one side (rabb al-mal) and work from the other (mudarib). The legal status of the mudarib is multi-faceted: he is a trustee (amin) over the capital, an agent (wakil) in transactions, a partner (sharik) in profit, but if the contract becomes corrupt (fasid), he is a hired worker (ajir), and if he violates terms, he becomes a usurper (ghasib). If the mudarib stipulates all profit for himself, the contract is not mudarabah but essentially a loan (qard). The text then explains that profit sharing can be unequal, but if two people provide capital equally, they must share surplus profit equally. The pillar (rukn) is the verbal expression indicating mudarabah, such as 'I gave you this capital as mudarabah' or similar phrases. A mere command to buy with profit share without specifying mudarabah terms results in a void ijarah. Conditions include that capital must be in a known quantity of coins (thaman). If there is a dispute over capital at profit division, the mudarib's statement is taken with oath, but the owner's evidence is preferred. The text also covers mudarabah with debt: when the debt is owed by the mudarib himself, the contract is invalid; when owed by a third party, it is valid but disliked. There are subtle distinctions in the particles used (thumma, fa, waw) that determine when the mudarib may begin trading. Finally, it mentions that if the owner tells a usurper, depositary, or bailee to work with the property, it is permissible.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudarabah): A partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides work, with profit shared as agreed.
مضارب (mudarib): The working partner who manages the capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the legal status of the mudarib when he acts within the contract's terms?
A) Hired worker
B) Usurper
C) Trustee and agent
D) Borrower

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah is a permissible partnership in profit, and the mudarib's legal status varies with his actions: trustee, agent, partner, hired worker, or usurper.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
intermediate

Profit Sharing and Conditions in Mudarabah
Rulings on profit sharing and the pillar of mudarabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rules of profit disparity and identify the correct expression for a valid mudarabah.

Core Idea
Profit shares can be unequal, but when capital is equal, surplus profit must be shared equally.

This lesson delves into the profit-sharing mechanism. The Hanafi school allows disparity in profit shares as long as both parties agree. However, if multiple people provide equal capital, the surplus profit must be divided equally. The lesson also covers the essential expression (rukn) and distinguishes mudarabah from a void ijarah.

Guided Path
1
Understand profit disparity
The text states that disparity in profit is permissible. For example, one party may get two-thirds and the other one-third of the profit.
2
Analyze the equal capital rule
If two people provide capital equally, any surplus profit after returning the capital must be divided equally, even if they stipulated otherwise. This is because equality in capital implies equality in profit.
3
Identify the pillar (rukn)
The pillar is the verbal expression (lafz). Examples given: 'I gave you this capital as mudarabah', 'take this and work with it on condition that you have half the profit', etc.
4
Distinguish from void ijarah
A mere command to buy with a profit share without a clear mudarabah expression results in a void ijarah (fāsid), entitling the worker to an equivalent wage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة هي شركة بمال من جانب وعمل من جانب والمضارب أمين وبالتصرف وكيل وبالربح شريك وبالفساد أجير وبالخلاف غاصب وباشتراط كل الربح له مستقرض كتاب المضاربة (هي شركة في الربح بمال من جانب وعمل من جانب فلو شرط كل الربح لأحدهما لا يكون مضاربة. ويجوز التفاوت في الربح وإذا كان المال من اثنين فلا بد من تساويهما فيما فضل من الربح حتى لو شرط لأحدهما الثلثان وللآخر الثلث فيما فضل فهو بينهما نصفين لاستوائهما في رأس المال وركنها اللفظ الدال عليها كقوله دفعت إليك هذا المال مضاربة أو مفاوضة أو معاملة أو خذ هذا المال واعمل به على أن لك من الربح نصفه أو ثلثه، أو قال ابتع به متاعاً فما كان من فضل فلك كذا، أو خذ ذلك بالنصف بخلاف خذ هذه الألف واشتر بها هروياً بالنصف ولم يزد عليه فليس بمضاربة بل إجارة فاسدة له أجر مثله إن اشترى وليس له البيع إلا بأمر . وشرطها أن يكون رأس المال الأثمان من وهو معلوم ويكفي الإعلام بالإشارة، فإن اختلفا في مقدار رأس المال عند قسمة الربح فالقول للمضارب مع يمينه والبينة لرب المال . وأما المضاربة بدين فإن كان على المضارب فلا يصح وما اشتراه له والدين في ذمته، وإن كان على غيره بأن قال اقبض مالي على فلان ثم اعمل به مضاربة فهو جائز وإن كان مكروهاً لأنه شرط لنفسه منفعة قبل العقد كما في المبسوط . ولو قال اقبض ديني على فلان ثم اعمل به مضاربة فعمل قبل أن يقبض كله ،ضمن ولو قال فاعمل به لا يضمن . وكذا بالواو لأن ثم للترتيب فلا يكون مأذوناً بالعمل إلا بعد قبض الكل بخلاف الفاء والواو فإنه يكفي قبل القبض ولو قال اقبض ديني لتعمل به مضاربة لا يكون مأذوناً ما لم يقبض الكل. ولو قال اشتر لي عبداً بنسيئة ثم بعه واعمل بثمنه مضاربة فاشتراه ثم باعه وعمل فيه جاز. ولو قال رب المال للغاصب أو المستودع أو المبضع اعمل بما في يدك
Book of Mudarabah: It is a company with capital from one side and work from the other. The mudarib is a trustee, and regarding disposition he is an agent, and in profit he is a partner, and in case of corruption he is a hired worker, and in case of violation he is a usurper, and if all profit is stipulated for him, he is a borrower. Book of Mudarabah (It is a partnership in profit with capital from one side and work from the other. If all profit is stipulated for one of them, it is not mudarabah. Disparity in profit is permissible. If the capital is from two, then they must be equal in the surplus profit; so if one stipulates two-thirds and the other one-third of the surplus, it is half and half because they are equal in capital. Its pillar is the expression indicating it, like saying: I gave you this capital as mudarabah, or mufawada, or mu'amala, or take this capital and work with it on condition that you have half or one-third of the profit, or he said: buy goods with it, and whatever profit there is, you have such-and-such, or take that for half. Unlike: take these thousand and buy with them Herawi cloth for half, and did not add more; that is not mudarabah but a void contract of hire, and he is entitled to his equivalent wage if he buys, and he has no right to sell except by order. Its condition is that the capital be from coins (thaman) and it be known, and it is sufficient to indicate it by pointing. If they differ in the amount of capital at the time of dividing profit, the word is of the mudarib with his oath, and the evidence is for the owner of capital. As for mudarabah with a debt: if it is on the mudarib, it is not valid, and whatever he buys is for him and the debt remains in his liability. If it is on someone else, such as he said: collect my money from so-and-so then work with it as mudarabah, it is permissible although disliked because he stipulated a benefit for himself before the contract, as in al-Mabsut. If he said: collect my debt from so-and-so then work with it as mudarabah, and he worked before collecting all of it, he guarantees. If he said: 'fa'lam bihi' (then work with it) he does not guarantee. Likewise with 'waw' because 'thumma' implies sequence, so he is not permitted to work except after collecting all; contrary to 'fa' and 'waw', they suffice before collection. If he said: collect my debt to work with it as mudarabah, he is not permitted until he collects all. If he said: buy for me a slave on credit, then sell him and work with his price as mudarabah, and he bought, then sold, and worked with it, it is permissible. If the owner of capital said to a usurper, a depositary, or a bailee: work with what is in your hand...
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the Book of Mudarabah, providing a comprehensive definition and many rulings. Mudarabah is defined as a company (sharika) in profit: capital from one side (rabb al-mal) and work from the other (mudarib). The legal status of the mudarib is multi-faceted: he is a trustee (amin) over the capital, an agent (wakil) in transactions, a partner (sharik) in profit, but if the contract becomes corrupt (fasid), he is a hired worker (ajir), and if he violates terms, he becomes a usurper (ghasib). If the mudarib stipulates all profit for himself, the contract is not mudarabah but essentially a loan (qard). The text then explains that profit sharing can be unequal, but if two people provide capital equally, they must share surplus profit equally. The pillar (rukn) is the verbal expression indicating mudarabah, such as 'I gave you this capital as mudarabah' or similar phrases. A mere command to buy with profit share without specifying mudarabah terms results in a void ijarah. Conditions include that capital must be in a known quantity of coins (thaman). If there is a dispute over capital at profit division, the mudarib's statement is taken with oath, but the owner's evidence is preferred. The text also covers mudarabah with debt: when the debt is owed by the mudarib himself, the contract is invalid; when owed by a third party, it is valid but disliked. There are subtle distinctions in the particles used (thumma, fa, waw) that determine when the mudarib may begin trading. Finally, it mentions that if the owner tells a usurper, depositary, or bailee to work with the property, it is permissible.

Key Terms
فضل الربح (fadl al-ribh): The surplus profit after returning the capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the pillar (rukn) of mudarabah according to this text?
A) Capital
B) Work
C) Profit
D) The expression indicating the contract

Key Takeaway
Profit sharing can be unequal, but if capital is equal, surplus profit must be divided equally, and the expression is the essential pillar.

Conditions of Capital in Mudarabah
Conditions of capital and dispute resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of the capital in mudarabah and resolve disputes over its amount.

Core Idea
The capital must be known and in coins; if disputed, the mudarib's word is taken with oath.

This lesson covers the specific conditions of the capital in a mudarabah contract. The Hanafi school requires that the capital be in the form of coins (thaman) and be known (ma'lum). If a dispute arises about the amount, the mudarib's statement is preferred with his oath, but the owner's evidence is stronger if produced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions of capital
The text states two conditions: capital must be from coins (thaman) and it must be known. It can be indicated by pointing.
2
Understand the dispute resolution rule
If they differ in the amount of capital at the time of profit distribution, the mudarib's word is taken with his oath. But if the owner brings evidence, that evidence prevails.

Source Text

كتاب المضاربة هي شركة بمال من جانب وعمل من جانب والمضارب أمين وبالتصرف وكيل وبالربح شريك وبالفساد أجير وبالخلاف غاصب وباشتراط كل الربح له مستقرض كتاب المضاربة (هي شركة في الربح بمال من جانب وعمل من جانب فلو شرط كل الربح لأحدهما لا يكون مضاربة. ويجوز التفاوت في الربح وإذا كان المال من اثنين فلا بد من تساويهما فيما فضل من الربح حتى لو شرط لأحدهما الثلثان وللآخر الثلث فيما فضل فهو بينهما نصفين لاستوائهما في رأس المال وركنها اللفظ الدال عليها كقوله دفعت إليك هذا المال مضاربة أو مفاوضة أو معاملة أو خذ هذا المال واعمل به على أن لك من الربح نصفه أو ثلثه، أو قال ابتع به متاعاً فما كان من فضل فلك كذا، أو خذ ذلك بالنصف بخلاف خذ هذه الألف واشتر بها هروياً بالنصف ولم يزد عليه فليس بمضاربة بل إجارة فاسدة له أجر مثله إن اشترى وليس له البيع إلا بأمر . وشرطها أن يكون رأس المال الأثمان من وهو معلوم ويكفي الإعلام بالإشارة، فإن اختلفا في مقدار رأس المال عند قسمة الربح فالقول للمضارب مع يمينه والبينة لرب المال . وأما المضاربة بدين فإن كان على المضارب فلا يصح وما اشتراه له والدين في ذمته، وإن كان على غيره بأن قال اقبض مالي على فلان ثم اعمل به مضاربة فهو جائز وإن كان مكروهاً لأنه شرط لنفسه منفعة قبل العقد كما في المبسوط . ولو قال اقبض ديني على فلان ثم اعمل به مضاربة فعمل قبل أن يقبض كله ،ضمن ولو قال فاعمل به لا يضمن . وكذا بالواو لأن ثم للترتيب فلا يكون مأذوناً بالعمل إلا بعد قبض الكل بخلاف الفاء والواو فإنه يكفي قبل القبض ولو قال اقبض ديني لتعمل به مضاربة لا يكون مأذوناً ما لم يقبض الكل. ولو قال اشتر لي عبداً بنسيئة ثم بعه واعمل بثمنه مضاربة فاشتراه ثم باعه وعمل فيه جاز. ولو قال رب المال للغاصب أو المستودع أو المبضع اعمل بما في يدك
Book of Mudarabah: It is a company with capital from one side and work from the other. The mudarib is a trustee, and regarding disposition he is an agent, and in profit he is a partner, and in case of corruption he is a hired worker, and in case of violation he is a usurper, and if all profit is stipulated for him, he is a borrower. Book of Mudarabah (It is a partnership in profit with capital from one side and work from the other. If all profit is stipulated for one of them, it is not mudarabah. Disparity in profit is permissible. If the capital is from two, then they must be equal in the surplus profit; so if one stipulates two-thirds and the other one-third of the surplus, it is half and half because they are equal in capital. Its pillar is the expression indicating it, like saying: I gave you this capital as mudarabah, or mufawada, or mu'amala, or take this capital and work with it on condition that you have half or one-third of the profit, or he said: buy goods with it, and whatever profit there is, you have such-and-such, or take that for half. Unlike: take these thousand and buy with them Herawi cloth for half, and did not add more; that is not mudarabah but a void contract of hire, and he is entitled to his equivalent wage if he buys, and he has no right to sell except by order. Its condition is that the capital be from coins (thaman) and it be known, and it is sufficient to indicate it by pointing. If they differ in the amount of capital at the time of dividing profit, the word is of the mudarib with his oath, and the evidence is for the owner of capital. As for mudarabah with a debt: if it is on the mudarib, it is not valid, and whatever he buys is for him and the debt remains in his liability. If it is on someone else, such as he said: collect my money from so-and-so then work with it as mudarabah, it is permissible although disliked because he stipulated a benefit for himself before the contract, as in al-Mabsut. If he said: collect my debt from so-and-so then work with it as mudarabah, and he worked before collecting all of it, he guarantees. If he said: 'fa'lam bihi' (then work with it) he does not guarantee. Likewise with 'waw' because 'thumma' implies sequence, so he is not permitted to work except after collecting all; contrary to 'fa' and 'waw', they suffice before collection. If he said: collect my debt to work with it as mudarabah, he is not permitted until he collects all. If he said: buy for me a slave on credit, then sell him and work with his price as mudarabah, and he bought, then sold, and worked with it, it is permissible. If the owner of capital said to a usurper, a depositary, or a bailee: work with what is in your hand...

Mudarabah with Debt and Special Scenarios
Mudarabah with debt and particle distinctions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid mudarabah with debt and apply the nuances of particles thumma, fa, and waw.

Core Idea
Mudarabah with debt on the mudarib is invalid; with debt on a third party, it's valid but disliked; the particle 'thumma' requires full collection before work.

This lesson covers mudarabah where the capital is a debt. The Hanafi school differentiates between debt owed by the mudarib himself and debt owed by others. It also delves into the subtle effects of Arabic particles (thumma, fa, waw) on permissibility of starting work before collecting the debt.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish debt on mudarib vs on third party
If the debt is on the mudarib himself, the contract is invalid because he would be using his own debt as capital. If the debt is on a third party, it is valid but disliked because it benefits the owner before the contract.
2
Analyze the particle effect
If the owner says 'thumma' (then), the mudarib must collect the entire debt before working. If 'fa' or 'waw' is used, he may start after partial collection. 'Thumma' implies sequence and delay.
3
Apply the rule to the 'buy on credit' scenario
If the owner says 'buy a slave on credit, then sell him, then work with the price as mudarabah', it is valid.
4
Apply to usurper/depositary/bailee
If the owner tells a usurper, depositary, or bailee to work with what is in his hand, it is permissible.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
beginner
6 min
Definition and Valid Wording of Mudarabah
Defines mudarabah and clarifies valid contract expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of mudarabah, identify the conditions for valid profit sharing, and distinguish valid contract wordings from invalid ones.

Core Idea
Mudarabah is a partnership in profit: one provides capital, the other labor; profit shares must be clearly defined from the surplus.

Mudarabah is a foundational contract in Islamic finance, allowing capital providers and entrepreneurs to share profits. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq defines mudarabah and clarifies key conditions—especially how profit must be shared from the surplus, and what wordings make the contract valid or invalid.

Guided Path
1
Deconstruct the definition
Identify the two parties: one provides capital (rabb al-mal), the other provides labor (mudarib). Profit is shared according to agreement.
Mudarabah is a 'شركة في الربح' (partnership in profit), not in capital.
2
Apply the all-profit condition
If either party stipulates all profit for themselves, the contract is not mudarabah. Understand why: profit sharing must be mutual.
This invalidates the contract entirely; it becomes something else.
3
Apply the equal-capital rule
When both parties provide capital, they must share the surplus profit equally regardless of stipulated ratios, because their capital contributions are equal.
Example: if capital is equal, even if one stipulates 2/3 and the other 1/3, the actual division is 1/2 each.
4
Recognize the rukn (pillar)
The pillar of mudarabah is the verbal expression indicating the contract. Memorize the valid phrases listed in the passage.
Phrases like 'دفعت إليك مضاربة' or 'خذ هذا المال واعمل به على أن لك نصف الربح' are valid.
5
Distinguish valid from invalid wordings
Some statements sound like mudarabah but are not. The passage gives the example 'خذ هذه الألف واشتر بها هروياً بالنصف' without specifying a profit share from surplus, which makes it a void lease (ijarah fasidah).
The key difference: mudarabah requires a share of surplus profit; a fixed wage or ambiguous statement makes it ijarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة هي شركة في الربح بمال من جانب وعمل من جانب فلو شرط كل الربح لأحدهما لا يكون مضاربة. ويجوز التفاوت في الربح وإذا كان المال من اثنين فلا بد من تساويهما فيما فضل من الربح حتى لو شرط لأحدهما الثلثان وللآخر الثلث فيما فضل فهو بينهما نصفين لاستوائهما في رأس المال وركنها اللفظ الدال عليها كقوله دفعت إليك هذا المال مضاربة أو مفاوضة أو معاملة أو خذ هذا المال واعمل به على أن لك من الربح نصفه أو ثلثه، أو قال ابتع به متاعاً فما كان من فضل فلك كذا، أو خذ ذلك بالنصف بخلاف خذ هذه الألف واشتر بها هروياً بالنصف ولم يزد عليه فليس بمضاربة بل إجارة فاسدة له أجر مثله إن اشترى وليس له البيع إلا بأمر.
The book of mudarabah. It is a partnership in profit with capital from one side and work from one side. If all profit is stipulated for one of them, it is not mudarabah. Disparity in profit is permissible. When capital is from two persons, they must be equal in the surplus profit; so if one is stipulated two-thirds and the other one-third of the surplus, it is half and half between them due to their equality in capital. Its pillar (rukn) is the expression indicating it, such as his statement: 'I have paid this capital to you as mudarabah, or mufawadah, or mu'amalah,' or 'Take this capital and work with it on the condition that you have half or one-third of the profit,' or he said: 'Buy goods with it, and whatever surplus there is, you have such-and-such,' or 'Take it for half.' Unlike: 'Take this thousand and buy herbs with it for half' without adding more; that is not mudarabah but rather a void lease (ijarah fasidah), for which he gets the equivalent wage if he buys, and he has no right to sell except by command.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on mudarabah (silent partnership) by defining it as a partnership in profit where one party provides capital (rabb al-mal) and the other provides labor (mudarib). The author immediately clarifies a key condition: if either party stipulates all profit for themselves, the contract is not mudarabah. Profit may be shared unequally if the capital is from one side; but if both provide capital, they must share the surplus profit equally regardless of their stipulated ratios, because they are equal in capital contribution. The pillar (rukn) of the contract is the verbal offer and acceptance using specific phrases like 'دفعت إليك مضاربة' or 'خذ هذا المال واعمل به على أن لك من الربح نصفه'. The author contrasts valid mudarabah wordings with invalid ones: if someone says 'خذ هذه الألف واشتر بها هروياً بالنصف' without specifying a profit share, it is not mudarabah but a void hire contract (ijarah fasidah), where the worker deserves the market wage for his work but has no right to sell without permission. This distinction highlights the necessity of clearly defining profit shares.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudarabah): A partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit shared according to agreement.
ركن (rukn): The essential pillar of the contract, which is the verbal expression (ijab wa qabul).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if two people both provide capital in a mudarabah and stipulate that one gets two-thirds of the profit and the other gets one-third?
A) The stipulated shares are valid because they agreed.
B) The profit is divided equally because they are equal in capital.
C) The contract becomes void because profit cannot be unequal.
D) The one who gets two-thirds must compensate the other.

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah requires a clear definition of profit shares from the surplus, and the contract is invalid if all profit goes to one party or the wording is ambiguous.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing
advanced
15 min
Conditions and Subsidiary Rulings of Mudarabah
Lists six conditions and subsidiary rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions of a valid mudarabah, identify conditions that invalidate the contract, and explain the mudarib's legal capacities.

Core Idea
Six conditions ensure mudarabah is free from uncertainty; violation invalidates the contract or voids the condition.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq systematically presents the conditions for a valid mudarabah contract according to the Hanafi school. It also discusses special cases such as mudarabah with debt, the effect of invalid stipulations, and the mudarib's multiple legal roles. Understanding these details is essential for structuring lawful profit-sharing arrangements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six conditions
Read the passage carefully and list each condition explicitly mentioned by the author. These include the nature and knowledge of capital, delivery, profit sharing, and the mudarib's share source.
The conditions are numbered (third, fourth, fifth, sixth) but the first two appear at the beginning.
2
Understand the thaman requirement
The capital must be in gold or silver coins (thaman) or bullion that circulates as currency. This excludes merchandise or other commodities.
Cross-madhhab: Shafi'is allow any valuable property.
3
Analyze the debt scenarios
If the debt is owed by the mudarib, the contract is invalid. If owed by a third party, it is valid but disliked if the instruction uses 'thumma' meaning sequence.
The words thumma vs fa/waw affect permission to work before full collection.
4
Recognize invalid stipulations
Conditions that cause ignorance of profit (jahalah) invalidate the contract. Stipulating loss on the mudarib or giving him a share from capital are void conditions, but the contract remains valid.
The contract becomes fasid (corrupt), not batil; the mudarib gets wages.
5
Trace the mudarib's capacities
The mudarib is a trustee after delivery, agent at work, partner at profit, and hired worker if the contract is corrupt. Special cases like guardian, ma'dhun, and mukatab have additional rules.
The mudarib may sell on credit, travel, hire workers, but cannot marry off slaves.

وباشتراطه لرب المال مستبضع وإنما تصح بما تصح به الشركة ويكون الربح بينهما مشاعاً وإن شرط لأحدهما زيادة عشرة فله أجر مثله ولا يجاوز عن المشروط وكل شرط يوجب جهالة الربح يفسده وإلا لا ويبطل الشرط كشرط الوضيعة على المضارب ويدفع . درهم مضاربة بالنصف جاز الثالث أن يكون رأس المال مسلماً إلى المضارب بخلاف الشركة . الرابع أن يكون الربح بينهما شائعاً كالنصف والثلث لا سهماً معيناً يقطع الشركة كمائة أو مع النصف عشرة. الخامس أن يكون نصيب كل منهما معلوماً فكل شرط يؤدي إلى جهالة الربح فهي فاسدة وما لا فلا مثل أن يشترط أن تكون الوضيعة على المضارب أو عليهما فهي صحيحة وهو باطل. السادس أن يكون المشروط للمضارب مشروطاً من الربح حتى لو شرطا له شيئاً من رأس المال أو منه ومن الربح فسدت وحكمها أنه أمين بعد دفع المال إليه، ووكيل عند العمل وشريك عند الربح ، وأجير عند الفساد فله أجر مثله والربح كله لرب المال إلا في الوصي إذا أخذ مال الصغير مضاربة وشرط لنفسه عشرة دراهم فإنه لا أجر له إذا عمل ؛ كذا في أحكام الصغار ولا ضمان عليه إذا فسدت بالهلاك بغير صنعه، وغاصب عند الخلاف، ومستقرض عند اشتراط كل الربح ،له ومستبضع عند اشتراطه لرب المال فلا له ولا أجر ولا ضمان عليه بالهلاك وإنما تصح بما تصح به الشركة وهي الدراهم ربح والدنانير إلا الفلوس النافقة . المال مع وأما التبر فإن كان في موضع بروج به كالأثمان تجوز به وإلا فلا كالمكيل والموزون . ولو دفع إليه عرضاً وقال بعه وأعمل بثمنه مضاربة جاز، وشرط العمل على رب المال لا يصح سواء كان المالك عاقداً أو غير عاقد كالصغير والمعتوه، وكذا أحد الشريكين إذا دفع المال مضاربة بشرط أن يعمل شريكه مع المضارب إن كان المال من شركتهما وإلا فهي جائزة إن كانت شركة عنان، وإن كانت مفاوضة لا تصح مطلقاً. وإذا شرط أن يتصرف في المضارب فإن كان العاقد ليس أهلاً للمضاربة في ذلك المال تفسد كالمأذون إذا دفع مضاربة وشرط عمله مع المضارب، وإن كان العاقد ممن يجوز يأخذ ماله مضاربة لم تفسد كالأب والوصي إذا دفعا مال الصغير مضاربة وشرطا عملهما معه بجزء من الربح، وإن شرط المأذون عمل مولاه فسدت إن لم يكن عليه دين وإلا صحت كالمكاتب إذا شرط عمل مطلقاً (ويبيع) المضارب في المضاربة الصحيحة (بالنقد والنسيئة ويشتري مولاه فإنه يصح ماله ويوكل ويسافر براً وبحراً ولو دفع إليه في بلدة على الظاهر ويأذن لعبد المضاربة في التجارة الأمة ولا يزوج عبداً ولا أمة كالشريك عناناً ومفاوضة بخلاف الأب والوصي يملكان تزويج وله الإيضاع والإيداع واستئجار العمال للأعمال واستئجار المنازل لحفظ الأموال واستئجار المنازل لحفظ الأموال عبارة الذخيرة من الفصل التاسع: وكذلك يستأجر المضارب البيوت لحفظ الأموال .
And its condition is that the capital is from silver/gold coins (thaman) and is known, and informing by pointing suffices. If they differ on the amount of capital at the time of profit distribution, the mudarib's statement is accepted with his oath, and evidence is for the capital owner. As for mudarabah with a debt: if it is owed by the mudarib, it is invalid; what he buys is for him and the debt remains in his liability. If it is owed by another, such as saying 'Collect my money from so-and-so then work with it as mudarabah,' it is permissible but disliked because he stipulates a benefit for himself before the contract, as in al-Mabsut. If he says 'Collect my debt from so-and-so then work with it as mudarabah' and he works before collecting all of it, he is liable. If he says 'then work with it' (with fa), he is not liable. Similarly with waw, because 'thumma' implies sequence, so he is not permitted to work until after collecting all; contrary to 'fa' and 'waw', which suffice before collection. If he says 'Collect my debt to work with it as mudarabah,' he is not permitted until he collects all. If he says 'Buy a slave for me on credit, then sell him and work with his price as mudarabah,' and he buys, then sells, and works with it, it is valid. If the capital owner says to a usurper, depositee, or bailee 'Work with what is in your hand' and stipulates it for the capital owner as a loan (mustabdi'), it is only valid with what partnership is valid with, and profit is shared jointly. If he stipulates an extra ten for one of them, he gets the equivalent wage but does not exceed the stipulated. Every condition that causes ignorance of profit invalidates the contract; otherwise not, and the condition is void, like stipulating loss (wadi'ah) on the mudarib. ... [continues] ... And its ruling: he is a trustee after delivery of capital, an agent at work, a partner at profit, and a hired worker when the contract is corrupt, so he gets the equivalent wage, and all profit is for the capital owner, except in the case of a guardian who takes the minor's money as mudarabah and stipulates ten dirhams for himself; then he gets no wage if he works, as in Ahkam al-Sighar. And there is no liability on him if the contract becomes corrupt due to destruction without his act. He is a usurper in case of disagreement, a borrower if all profit is stipulated for him, and a bailee (mustabdi') if all profit is stipulated for the capital owner; so he gets nothing, no wage, and no liability for destruction. It is only valid with what partnership is valid with, which is dirhams and dinars, except current fals (copper coins). As for bullion (tibr), if it is in a place where it circulates like coins, it is permissible; otherwise not, like measured and weighed items. If he gives him merchandise and says 'Sell it and work with its price as mudarabah,' it is valid. Stipulating work on the capital owner is invalid, whether the owner is a contracting party or not, such as a minor or insane person. Similarly, if one of two partners gives capital as mudarabah on condition that his partner works with the mudarib: if the capital is from their partnership, it is invalid; otherwise it is valid if it is a partnership of 'inan, but if it is mufawadah, it is absolutely invalid. If he stipulates that he himself transacts in the mudarabah: if the contracting party is not eligible for mudarabah in that capital, the contract becomes corrupt, like a permitted slave (ma'dhun) who gives mudarabah and stipulates his own work with the mudarib. If the contracting party is eligible to take his capital as mudarabah, it is not corrupt, like a father or guardian who gives the minor's capital as mudarabah and stipulates their own work with him for a share of the profit. If the ma'dhun stipulates the work of his master, it becomes corrupt if the ma'dhun has no debt; otherwise it is valid, like a mukatab who stipulates work absolutely. The mudarib in a valid mudarabah sells for cash and credit, and buys, and his master's money becomes valid. He can appoint an agent, travel by land and sea, even if the capital was given to him in a town, according to the apparent view. He can permit the slave of the mudarabah to trade, but he cannot marry a slave or slave-girl, like a partner in 'inan or mufawadah, contrary to the father and guardian who have the power to marry. He can entrust (ida'), deposit, hire workers for tasks, and hire houses for keeping money, as in the expression of al-Dhakhira from the ninth chapter: 'Likewise, the mudarib may hire houses for keeping money.'
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a detailed listing of the conditions (shurut) for a valid mudarabah contract and related rulings. The author begins by stating that capital must be in the form of gold or silver coins (thaman) and must be known; pointing to the capital is sufficient for identification. If the capital amount is disputed at profit distribution, the mudarib's word is taken with his oath because he is the trustee, but the owner can provide evidence. The next section discusses mudarabah with debt: if the debt is owed by the mudarib himself, the contract is invalid because the capital is not delivered; any purchase becomes his own. If the debt is owed by a third party, the contract is permissible if the mudarib is instructed to collect the debt first and then work with it, but using 'thumma' (then) requires collection before work. Using 'fa' or 'waw' permits work before full collection. The conditions are then enumerated: (1) capital must be thaman (gold/silver), (2) capital must be known, (3) capital must be delivered to the mudarib, (4) profit must be shared as a common fraction (shayi'), not a fixed sum, (5) each party's share must be known, and (6) the mudarib's share must be from the profit, not from capital. Stipulations that cause ignorance (jahalah) invalidate the contract. The passage also describes the various capacities of the mudarib: trustee before profit, agent during work, partner when profit appears, and hired worker if the contract is corrupt. Special cases like the guardian of an orphan, the ma'dhun, and the mukatab are explained. Finally, the powers of the mudarib are listed: he can sell for cash and credit, travel, hire, and deposit, but cannot marry off slaves without permission, except for father/guardian. The source cites al-Dhakhira for the ruling on hiring houses.

Key Terms
رأس المال (ra's al-mal): The capital provided by the investor in a mudarabah; must be in the form of gold/silver coins (thaman) according to Hanafi.
وضيعة (wadi'ah): Loss in the mudarabah venture. Stipulating that loss falls on the mudarib is a void condition, but the contract remains valid.
مستبضع (mustabdi'): A type of mudarabah where the mudarib is merely a bailee and receives no share of profit; all profit goes to the capital owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if the capital owner stipulates that the mudarib bears all losses?
A) The contract becomes batil (void).
B) The contract is valid but the condition is void.
C) The mudarib is liable for losses.
D) The capital owner must compensate the mudarib.

Key Takeaway
Mudarabah requires six conditions; violating certain conditions invalidates the contract (fasid), while others only void the stipulation, preserving the contract with standard rulings.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Six Conditions and Legal Status of Mudarabah
Lists six conditions for mudarabah validity and mudarib's legal capacities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for a valid mudarabah, distinguish conditions that invalidate from those that are merely void, and explain the mudarib's legal status as amin, wakil, sharik, and ajir.

Core Idea
Valid mudarabah requires known profit shares, delivered capital, and no fixed profit; the mudarib is a trustee, agent, partner, or hireling depending on context.

Mudarabah is a partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor. The Hanafi school lays out precise conditions to avoid uncertainty (gharar). This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq lists six conditions and explains the mudarib's multi-faceted legal identity, which changes with the contract's validity and phase of operation.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the six conditions
Identify each condition from the text: capital delivered to mudarib, profit shared commonly, each party's share known, mudarib's share from profit, etc. List them in order as presented.
The sixth condition is that the mudarib's share must be from profit, not capital.
2
Classify conditions by legal effect
Some conditions are essential (arkan) and their omission invalidates (batil). Conditions leading to ignorance of profit invalidate the contract (fasid). Harmless conditions (e.g., stipulating loss on mudarib) are void but the contract remains sahih.
Differentiate between mufsidat (invalidators) and void conditions that don't affect the core.
3
Analyze the mudarib's legal status
The mudarib is an amin (trustee) after receiving capital, a wakil (agent) when working, a sharik (partner) when profit accrues, and an ajir (hireling) if the contract is invalid. Understand the implications for liability and compensation.
In valid contract, no liability for losses beyond misconduct; in invalid contract, he gets ujr al-mithl.
4
Apply special cases
Consider the guardian's mudarabah with orphan's money (no wage if stipulates fixed amount), destruction without fault (no liability), and scenarios where mudarib becomes a usurper, borrower, or mustabdi'.
Each scenario changes the mudarib's status and liability.
5
Identify permissible capital types
Capital must be dirhams, dinars, or current fulus. Uncoined gold/silver if used as currency is allowed; weighed/measured goods are not. A commodity can be sold and its proceeds used for mudarabah.
The principle is that capital must be fungible and easily quantifiable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المضاربة وباشتراطه لرب المال مستبضع وإنما تصح بما تصح به الشركة ويكون الربح بينهما مشاعاً وإن شرط لأحدهما زيادة عشرة فله أجر مثله ولا يجاوز عن المشروط وكل شرط يوجب جهالة الربح يفسده وإلا لا ويبطل الشرط كشرط الوضيعة على المضارب ويدفع مضاربة بالنصف جاز الثالث أن يكون رأس المال مسلماً إلى المضارب بخلاف الشركة . الرابع أن يكون الربح بينهما شائعاً كالنصف والثلث لا سهماً معيناً يقطع الشركة كمائة أو مع النصف عشرة. الخامس أن يكون نصيب كل منهما معلوماً فكل شرط يؤدي إلى جهالة الربح فهي فاسدة وما لا فلا مثل أن يشترط أن تكون الوضيعة على المضارب أو عليهما فهي صحيحة وهو باطل. السادس أن يكون المشروط للمضارب مشروطاً من الربح حتى لو شرطا له شيئاً من رأس المال أو منه ومن الربح فسدت وحكمها أنه أمين بعد دفع المال إليه، ووكيل عند العمل وشريك عند الربح ، وأجير عند الفساد فله أجر مثله والربح كله لرب المال إلا في الوصي إذا أخذ مال الصغير مضاربة وشرط لنفسه عشرة دراهم فإنه لا أجر له إذا عمل ؛ كذا في أحكام الصغار ولا ضمان عليه إذا فسدت بالهلاك بغير صنعه، وغاصب عند الخلاف، ومستقرض عند اشتراط كل الربح له ومستبضع عند اشتراطه لرب المال فلا له ولا أجر ولا ضمان عليه بالهلاك وإنما تصح بما تصح به الشركة وهي الدراهم والدنانير إلا الفلوس النافقة . وأما التبر فإن كان في موضع بروج به كالأثمان تجوز به وإلا فلا كالمكيل والموزون . ولو دفع إليه عرضاً وقال بعه وأعمل بثمنه مضاربة جاز.
The book of Mudarabah. And by stipulating for the owner of capital that he is mustabdi'. And it is only valid by what makes shirkah valid, and the profit is shared between them in common. If they stipulate for one of them an extra ten, then he gets the equivalent wage but does not exceed the stipulated. Every condition that leads to ignorance of profit invalidates it, otherwise not. And the condition is void, like stipulating loss upon the mudarib. Mudarabah by half is valid. Third: that the capital be handed over to the mudarib, unlike shirkah. Fourth: that the profit be common between them like half or third, not a specific share that terminates the company like one hundred, or ten along with half. Fifth: that the share of each be known; so every condition leading to ignorance of profit is invalid, and what does not, is not; like stipulating that the loss be on the mudarib or on both, then it is valid but the condition is void. Sixth: that what is stipulated for the mudarib be stipulated from the profit, such that if they stipulate for him something from the capital or from both capital and profit, it is invalid. And its ruling: that he is a trustee after payment of the capital to him, and an agent at the time of work, and a partner at the time of profit, and a hireling at the time of invalidity, so he gets the wage of his like, and all profit goes to the owner of the capital, except for the guardian if he takes the orphan's money in mudarabah and stipulates for himself ten dirhams, then he gets no wage if he works; as in Ahkam al-Sighar. And there is no liability on him if it becomes invalid due to destruction without his act. And he is a usurper at the time of disagreement, and a borrower when all profit is stipulated for him, and an agent for purchase (mustabdi') when it is stipulated for the owner of capital, so he has nothing, no wage, and no liability upon destruction. And it is only valid by what makes shirkah valid, and that is dirhams and dinars except for current fulus. As for uncoined gold/silver, if it is in a place where it circulates like currency, it is permissible with it, otherwise not, like weighed and measured goods. And if he gives him a commodity and says 'Sell it and work with its price as mudarabah,' it is valid.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the foundational rules of mudarabah (qirad). It first addresses the conditions for validity: the capital must be handed over, profit must be shared in a known proportion (not a fixed sum), each party's share is known, and any condition leading to ignorance of profit invalidates the contract. However, a condition that does not affect profit knowledge (like loss on the mudarib) is void but the contract remains valid. Then it explains the legal status of the mudarib: after receiving capital, he is an amin (trustee); while working, he is an agent; at profit distribution, a partner; if the contract is invalid, he is a hireling entitled to wages. It also discusses special cases: a guardian taking orphan's money gets no wage if he stipulates, and the mudarib becomes a usurper or borrower in certain invalid scenarios. Finally, it covers permissible capital: dirhams, dinars, and even uncoined gold/silver if used as currency, but not weighed/measured goods. A commodity can be sold and its proceeds used for mudarabah.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudārabah): A partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profit shared as agreed.
مضارب (muḍārib): The party who manages the capital and labor; also called 'āmil.
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The capital provider; owner of the funds in the mudarabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a valid mudarabah contract, what happens if the parties stipulate that the mudarib will receive ten dirhams as his profit regardless of the actual profit?
A) The contract is valid and the mudarib gets ten dirhams.
B) The contract is void (batil).
C) The contract is valid but the stipulation is void, and the mudarib gets the equivalent wage (ujr al-mithl).
D) The contract becomes a loan (qard).

Key Takeaway
A valid mudarabah requires the capital to be delivered, a known common profit share, and the mudarib's share to be from profit; the mudarib's legal status shifts between trustee, agent, partner, and hireling depending on context.

Mudarib's Powers and Restrictions in Mudarabah
Rulings on valid/invalid stipulations and mudarib's powers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible and prohibited actions of a mudarib and identify the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on selling at non-customary prices.

Core Idea
The mudarib is like an agent: he must follow custom and explicit permission; exceeding limits makes him liable.

This lesson explores the detailed rules governing the mudarib's authority in a valid mudarabah contract. We will learn which stipulations regarding work are invalid, the scope of the mudarib's permissible actions, and the boundaries he must not cross. A key intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions on the validity of selling at a non-customary price reveals different approaches to the mudarib's discretion.

Guided Path
1
Identify invalid stipulations
Read the beginning of the passage to understand which stipulations regarding the owner's or partners' work invalidate the mudarabah. Note the exceptions (e.g., father/guardian).
Invalid stipulations: owner must work, partner must work with mudarib if money from shirkat mufawada, etc.
2
List the mudarib's permissible actions
Scan the long enumeration: selling, buying, travel, hiring, renting, pledging, etc. This shows the mudarib's broad agency powers.
They include actions normal for merchants; note the additions like pledging.
3
List the mudarib's prohibited actions
Identify actions not allowed: marrying slaves of mudarabah, mixing funds, borrowing without explicit permission, engaging in harmful or non-customary trade.
Prohibitions may not be absolute; some can be permitted by specific authorization.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Focus on the rule: buying at a price not normally overlooked is a violation. But when selling at such a price, Abu Hanifa says it is valid (like an unrestricted agent), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it invalid. Understand the basis and practical consequence.
This shows differing views on the mudarib's authority to deviate from custom.
5
Understand the effect of restrictive specifications
If the owner specifies place, good, or time, the mudarib must not exceed. Exceeding leads to liability. Returning to compliance restores mudarabah status.
Specifications are binding; 'act according to your opinion' does not negate core restrictions like borrowing.

جاز، وإن كان فيه ربح لا يجوز، ومتى جاز خرجت الجارية عن المضاربة. وليس له أن يشارك إلا أن يقول له اعمل برأيك ولو عقد مضاربة، وكذا ليس له أن يخلط مال المضاربة بماله ولا بمال غيره إلا أن يقول له اعمل برأيك. وليس له أن يعمل ما فيه ضرر ولا ما لا يعمله التجار ولا أن يبيع إلى أجل لا يبيعه التجار، وليس لأحد المضاربين أن يبيع أو يشتري بغير إذن صاحبه. ولو اشترى بيعاً فاسداً مما يملك بالقبض فليس بمخالف وما اشتراه على المضاربة. ولو اشترى بما لا يتغابن الناس في مثله يكون مخالفاً . سواء قيل له اعمل برأيك أو لا. ولو باع بهذه الصفة فهو جائز في قول أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما كالوكيل بالبيع المطلق، وليس له أن يقرض ولا أن يأخذ سفتجة ؛ كذا في الفتاوى الظهيرية. وله أن يحتال وإن كان الثاني أعسر من الأول ؛ كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان فالقرض والاستدانة لا يملكهما إلا بصريح الإذن. ولا يكفي قوله اعمل برأيك وإذا صرح بالاستدانة كانت شركة وجوه، وإذا اشترى بأكثر من المال كانت الزيادة له ولا يضمن بهذا الخلط الحكمي ولو كان المال دراهم فاشترى بغير الأثمان كان لنفسه وبالدنانير للمضاربة لأنهما جنس هنا. ولو كان في يده عرض لها فاشترى شيئاً لها لبيع العرض وينقد الثمن لم يجز حالاً كان الثمن أو مؤجلاً لأنه استدانة، ولا بد أن متاعاً يشتري في يده مثله من جنسه وصفته وقدره. ولا يملك المضارب في الفاسدة شيئاً . من ذلك إلا الإيداع؛ كذا في الفوائد التاجية ولم يتعد عما عينه إن كان التعيين مقيداً . من بلد وسلعة ووقت ومعامل كما في الشركة فإن تعدى صار ضامناً، فإذا اشترى بعده كان له ولو لم يشتر حتى عاد إلى الوفاق برئ من الضمان وعاد المال مضاربة، ولو عاد إليه في البعض كان مضاربة فيه اعتباراً للجزء بالكل، ولو كان التقييد غير مفيد قوله : (ولو عاد إليه في البعض أي إلى الوفاق في بعض المال كان مضاربة فيه أي في ذلك
Stipulating that the owner work is invalid, whether the owner is competent or not, like a minor or insane. Similarly, one of two partners paying money in mudarabah with condition that his partner work with the mudarib: if the money belongs to both, it is invalid; otherwise it is valid if it is a company of 'inan, but if mufawada it is invalid absolutely. And if he stipulates that he manage the mudarib? Then if the contracting party is not eligible to mudarabah with that money, it is invalid, like the ma'dhun if he pays mudarabah and stipulates his work with the mudarib. And if the contracting party is one who may take his money as mudarabah, it is not invalid, like the father and guardian if they pay the orphan's money as mudarabah and stipulate their work with him for a share of profit. And if the ma'dhun stipulates work of his master, it is invalid if he has no debt, otherwise valid, like the mukatab who stipulates work absolutely. (And the mudarib) in a valid mudarabah (sells) for cash and credit, buys, appoints agents, travels by land and sea, even if he gave it to him in a town apparently, and he authorizes the slave of mudarabah in trade? He does not marry a slave male or female like a partner in 'inan and mufawada, unlike the father and guardian who have the right to marry. And he has the right to place deposits, entrust, hire workers for tasks, rent houses for preserving wealth, rent houses for preserving wealth – phrase from al-Dhakhira from the ninth chapter: 'Likewise, the mudarib rents houses to preserve wealth.' And he does not marry? He sells for cash and credit, buys, appoints agents, travels, sends goods, deposits ships and animals, and he may give as collateral and take collateral, and he may rent uncultivated land and buy with part of the money food to plant it or plant date palms or trees. If he takes date palms or trees on mu'amalah (sharecropping) to spend on their pollination from the money, it is not valid. If he says 'act according to your opinion', he does not have the right to borrow; if he pawns anything from the mudarabah, he becomes liable. If the owner permits him, the debt is half on each. If the mudarib postpones the price, it is valid on the owner and he is not liable, unlike a special agent. If he reduces some of the price due to a defect complained by the buyer, and the reduction is his share or more but insignificant, it is valid; if the increase is not trivial, it is valid but he guarantees that from his own wealth to the owner, and the capital is what remains upon the buyer. It is prohibited for the mudarib to have intercourse with the mudarabah slave-girl and the like, even if the owner permits. If the mudarib marries a slave-girl by the owner's authorization, if there is no profit in the capital it is valid; if there is profit, it is not. And when it is valid, the slave-girl leaves the mudarabah. He may not partner unless the owner says 'act according to your opinion', even if he contracts a mudarabah. Similarly, he may not mix mudarabah funds with his own or with other funds unless told 'act according to your opinion'. He may not do what causes harm nor what merchants do not do, nor sell on a term that merchants do not. Neither mudarib may buy or sell without the other's permission. If he buys a corrupt sale which he can receive, it is not a violation; what he buys is for the mudarabah. If he buys at a price people would not normally overlook, it is a violation, whether told 'act according to your opinion' or not. If he sells in such a manner, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), like an unrestricted agent. He may not give a loan nor take a suftaja; as in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya. He may resort to trickery (hiyal) even if the second is poorer than the first; as in Fatawa Qadikhan. So loan and borrowing he does not possess except with explicit permission. And saying 'act according to your opinion' is not sufficient. If he explicitly permits borrowing, it becomes a partnership of faces (shirkat wujuh). If he buys for more than the capital, the excess belongs to him, and he is not liable for this constructive mixing. If the capital is dirhams and he buys with other than currency, it is for himself; with dinars, for the mudarabah because they are same genus here. If he has a commodity and buys something to sell the commodity and pay the price, it is not valid whether the price is immediate or deferred, because it is a loan. It must be that he buys goods in his possession of the same type, description, and quantity. The mudarib in an invalid contract does not possess any of that except depositing; as in al-Fawa'id al-Tajiyya. And he should not exceed what is specified if the specification is restrictive, regarding place, good, time, and transaction as in partnership. If he exceeds, he becomes liable. If he buys afterwards, it is for him; and if he does not buy until he returns to agreement, he is free from liability and the capital becomes mudarabah again. If he returns in part, it is mudarabah in that part, considering the part as the whole. And if the restriction is not beneficial? His statement: 'And if he returns to it in part' meaning if he returns to agreement in part of the capital, it is mudarabah in that part.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq details the restrictions on stipulations regarding work and the extensive powers of the mudarib in a valid mudarabah. It begins by stating that stipulating the owner to work is invalid, regardless of the owner's capacity. It then discusses scenarios where partners or guardians contract mudarabah with conditions. The main body enumerates the mudarib's authority: he can sell for cash or credit, buy, appoint agents, travel by land or sea, hire workers, rent storage, and even pledge property. However, he cannot marry slaves of the mudarabah, mix funds, borrow without permission, or engage in trade practices harmful or unusual. It also covers specific issues like price reductions, postponing payment, and buying on credit. Importantly, it records an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that selling at a price that is not commonly accepted is valid (like an unrestricted agent), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree. The passage concludes with rules on exceeding specified limits, liability, and returning to compliance. Throughout, the goal is to protect the capital and ensure the mudarib's actions are within customary trade practices.

Key Terms
شركة عنان (shirkat ‘inān): A partnership where each partner contributes capital and work, but not necessarily equal; they have limited liability.
شركة مفاوضة (shirkat mufāwaḍah): An unrestricted partnership where partners are equal in capital, authority, and liability.
المأذون (al-ma'dhūn): A slave permitted by his master to engage in trade; has limited capacity to enter contracts.
المضارب (al-muḍārib): The working partner in a mudarabah contract; the entrepreneur who manages the capital.
الاستدانة (al-istidānah): Borrowing money; taking a loan.
السفتجة (al-suf'taja): A letter of credit or bill of exchange used for transferring debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rule if the mudarib buys goods at a price that people would not normally overlook (i.e., a price that is not customary)?
A) He is always considered a violator and must compensate.
B) It is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but the two companions consider it a violation.
C) It is invalid regardless of permission.
D) He is not liable if he says 'act according to your opinion'.

Key Takeaway
In a valid mudarabah, the mudarib must operate within customary trade practices and explicit permissions; exceeding limits leads to liability, and there is an intra-Hanafi dispute on selling at non-customary prices.

Permissible Actions for the Mudarib
Lists permissible actions for the mudarib in a mudarabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the actions a mudarib may perform with mudarabah capital and identify which actions require explicit permission from the rabb al-mal.

Core Idea
The mudarib may sell, buy, hire, travel, and lease, but cannot borrow or pledge without explicit permission.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lists the scope of the mudarib's authority. Understanding these permissions is crucial for structuring valid mudarabah contracts and avoiding liability. The text distinguishes between actions that are automatically permitted and those that require the capital owner's express consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opening phrase
The phrase 'لا يزوج المال إلى المضارب' means the capital is not given in marriage to the mudarib, i.e., the mudarib does not receive ownership of the capital itself; he only has the right to use it for trade.
This sets the baseline: the mudarib is a trustee, not an owner.
2
List the trade and agency permissions
The mudarib may sell for cash and credit, buy goods, appoint an agent (tawkeel), travel with the capital, send goods via consignment (bida'a), and deposit goods in ships or on animals.
All these are standard trade-related actions.
3
Examine leasing and cultivation permissions
The mudarib may lease barren land (ard bayda') and buy seeds or plants with mudarabah funds to cultivate or plant date palms/trees. However, taking trees as mu'amala (sharecropping) with capital for pollination is not allowed.
Mu'amala is a separate contract; mixing it with mudarabah is impermissible.
4
Analyze the borrowing prohibition
Even if the rabb al-mal says 'act according to your opinion', the mudarib cannot borrow. If he borrows and pledges mudarabah assets, he becomes personally liable (damin).
General permission does not cover borrowing; it requires explicit consent.
5
Understand the effect of explicit permission
If the rabb al-mal explicitly authorizes borrowing, the debt is shared equally between them, removing the mudarib's personal liability.
This shows that borrowing liability can be apportioned by mutual agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يزوج المال إلى المضارب ويبيع بنقد ونسيئة ويشتري ويوكل ويسافر ويبضع ويودع السفن والدواب، وله أن يرهن ويرتهن لها وله أن يستأجر أرضاً بيضاء ويشتري ببعض المال طعاماً ليزرعها أو ليغرس فيها نخلاً أو شجراً. ولو أخذ نخلاً أو شجراً معاملة على أن ينفق في تلقيحها أو تأبيرها من المال لم يجز عليها وإن قال له اعمل برأيك ولا يملك الاستدانة فإن رهن شيئاً من المضاربة ضمن ، ولو أذنه رب المال في ذلك كان الدين عليهما نصفين
The capital is not given in marriage to the mudarib, and he sells for cash and credit, buys, appoints an agent, travels, consigns, and deposits in ships and riding animals. He may pledge and accept pledges for it, and may lease a barren land and buy with part of the capital food to cultivate it or to plant date palms or trees. If he takes date palms or trees as a mu'amala on condition that he spends on their pollination or fertilization from the capital, it is not permissible. And if he says to him 'act according to your opinion', he does not have the right to borrow. If he pledges something from the mudarabah, he becomes liable. If the owner of the capital permits him in that, the debt is upon both equally.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating the permissible actions for the mudarib (agent) in a mudarabah (silent partnership). The mudarib is authorized to sell both for cash and credit, buy goods, hire agents, travel with the capital, send goods via consignment (bida'a), deposit merchandise in ships or on animals, and engage in pledges (mortgage) both as pledgor and pledgee. He may also lease uncultivated land (ard bayda') and purchase seeds or plants from the mudarabah funds to cultivate it or to plant date palms and trees. However, there is a restriction: if he takes date palms or trees on a mu'amala (a sharecropping-like contract) with the condition that expenditure for pollination (talqih) or fertilization (ta'bir) comes from the mudarabah capital, it is not permissible (la yajuz) because such a contract resembles a partnership with uncertain terms. Even if the rabb al-mal (owner) says 'act according to your opinion' (i'mal bi-ra'yik), that general permission does not authorize borrowing (istidana). If the mudarib nonetheless borrows and pledges something from the mudarabah, he becomes personally liable (damin). However, if the rabb al-mal explicitly permits the borrowing, then the debt is shared equally between them (upon the rabb al-mal and the mudarib), indicating that the mudarib's personal liability is removed by permission only for that specific act.

Key Terms
مضاربة (mudarabah): A contract of silent partnership where one party (rabb al-mal) provides capital and the other (mudarib) provides labor and expertise, with profits shared as agreed.
يضارب (yudarib): The agent (mudarib) in the mudarabah contract.
استدانة (istidana): Borrowing money on behalf of the mudarabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the mudarib borrowing money without explicit permission from the rabb al-mal?
A) It is permissible because he has general authority.
B) It is not permissible, and if he does, he is personally liable.
C) It is permissible only with the condition of profit.
D) It is permissible if he pledges collateral.

Key Takeaway
The mudarib has broad authority for trade-related actions but cannot borrow or enter mu'amala with mudarabah capital without explicit permission; unauthorized borrowing makes him personally liable.
