Ruling on Mudaraba Slave Committing Manslaughter
Explaining distribution of ransom and service for a mudaraba slave's manslaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ransom distribution for a mudaraba slave who commits manslaughter and apply the conditions for surrender and ransom.

Core Idea
Ransom is a burden of ownership, divided proportionally; surrender requires both parties' presence.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the intricate fiqh of a mudaraba slave who kills by mistake. It sets out how the ransom and the slave's service are divided based on ownership shares, and carefully distinguishes between the procedures for surrendering the slave versus paying ransom. Understanding these rules reveals how Hanafi jurists balance the rights of the capital provider (owner) and the mudarib in a shared asset.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the parties' ownership shares
The mudarib invests 1000 dirhams for half-profit and buys a slave worth 2000. Determine the ownership: owner's capital (1000) + share of profit (500) = 1500 (3/4), mudarib's profit share (500) = 1/4.
If profit had not appeared, ownership would differ.
2
Apply the principle: ransom is a burden of ownership
Since ransom is a burden of ownership (mūnat al-mulk), it falls on each owner in proportion to their ownership share. Hence 3/4 on owner, 1/4 on mudarib.
This principle is the key proof (talil).
3
Determine the slave's service after ransom or surrender
Once the slave leaves the mudaraba (by ransom or surrender), he serves the owners in proportion to their former ownership shares.
Service is a residual obligation.
4
Analyze the condition for surrender: presence of both parties
Surrender (daf‘) requires the presence of both owner and mudarib because the mudarib has a right in the slave, analogous to a mortgagee's right in a mortgaged slave (qiyas).
Exception: if mudarib refuses and value equals capital, owner may surrender alone.
5
Distinguish ransom: presence not required, but voluntary payment
Ransom (fidā') does not require both parties to be present. If one party ransoms while the other is absent, he acts voluntarily and cannot recover the absent party's share.
Qadikhan holds that the mudarib alone cannot ransom either.

قوله : (معه ألف بالنصف فاشترى به عبداً قيمته ألفان فقتل رجلاً خطأ فثلاثة أرباع الفداء على المالك وربعه على المضارب والعبد يخدم المالك ثلاثة أيام والمضارب يوماً) لأن الفداء مؤنة الملك وقد كان الملك بينهما أرباعاً لأنه لما صار المال عيناً واحداً ظهر الربح وهو ألف بينهما وألف لرب المال، فإذا فدياه خرج العبد عن المضاربة لأن نصيب المضارب صار مضموناً عليه ونصيب رب المال صار له بقضاء القاضي بالفداء عليهما، وإذا خرج عنها بالدفع أو بالفداء يخدمهما على قدر ملكهما قيد بقوله قيمته ألفان لأنه لو كان قيمته ألفاً فتدبير الجناية إلى رب المال لأن الرقبة على ملكه لا ملك للمضارب فيها، فإن اختار رب الدفع واختار المضارب الفداء ذلك فله ذلك لأنه يستبقي بالفداء مال المضاربة وله ذلك لأن الربح يتوهم ؛ كذا في الإيضاح . ثم اعلم أن العبد المشتري في المضاربة إذا جنى خطأ لا يدفع بها حتى يحضر المضارب ورب المال سواء كان الأرش مثل قيمة العبد أو أقل أو أكثر، وكذا إذا كانت قيمته ألفاً لا غير لا يدفع إلا بحضرتهما لأن المضارب له فيه حق ليس لرب المال أن يأخذه ويمنعه عن بيعه كالمرهون إذا جنى خطأ لا يدفع إلا بحضرة الراهن والمرتهن. والحاصل أنه يشترط حضرة رب المال والمضارب للدفع دون الفداء إلا إذا أبي المضارب الدفع والفداء وقيمته مثل رأس المال فلرب المال دفعه لتعنته، فإن كان أحدهما غائباً وقيمة العبد ألفا درهم ففداه الحاضر كان متطوعاً لأنه أدى دين غيره بغير أمره وهو غير مضطر فيه، فإنه لو أقام البينة على الشركة لا يطالب بحصة صاحبه لا بالدفع ولا بالفداء؛ كذا في النهاية. وذكر قاضيخان أن المضارب ليس له الدفع والفداء وحده لأنه ليس من أحكام المضاربة فلهذا كان إليها
His statement: (He has one thousand dirhams half-profit, so with it he bought a slave worth two thousand, then the slave killed a man by mistake; so three-quarters of the ransom is upon the owner, one-quarter upon the mudarib, and the slave serves the owner three days and the mudarib one day) because the ransom is a burden of ownership, and ownership was between them fourths: because when the capital became one asset, the profit became apparent: one thousand, of which half is between them and one thousand for the owner. So if they ransom him, the slave leaves the mudaraba because the mudarib's share became guaranteed upon him, and the owner's share became his by the judge's decree of ransom upon them. And when the slave leaves by surrender or ransom, he serves them according to their share of ownership. He restricted by his saying 'worth two thousand' because if its value were one thousand, then the disposition of the injury belongs to the owner because the ownership is his, there being no ownership for the mudarib. If the owner chooses surrender and the mudarib chooses ransom, that is permissible for him because by ransom he preserves the mudaraba property, and for him because profit is expected; as in al-Idah. Then know that a slave purchased in mudaraba, if he commits manslaughter, he is not surrendered for it until the mudarib and the owner are present, whether the blood-money is equal to the slave's value or less or more. Likewise if his value is only one thousand, he is not surrendered except in their presence because the mudarib has a right in him; the owner may not take him and prevent his sale, like a mortgaged slave who commits manslaughter: he is not surrendered except in the presence of pledgor and pledgee. In summary, the presence of the owner and mudarib is required for surrender, not for ransom; except if the mudarib refuses both surrender and ransom and the value equals the capital, then the owner may surrender him due to his obstinacy. If one of them is absent and the slave's value is two thousand dirhams, and the present one ransoms, he is a volunteer because he paid another's debt without his order and he is not compelled, for if he established evidence of partnership, he does not demand his partner's share either for surrender or ransom; as in al-Nihaya. Qadikhan mentioned that the mudarib alone may not surrender or ransom because these are not among the rulings of mudaraba; so this is why...
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq concerning a mudaraba where the mudarib invests one thousand dirhams (half-profit) and buys a slave worth two thousand. The slave commits manslaughter (خطأ). The ruling distributes the ransom (فداء) and the slave's service according to ownership shares. The key principle is that the ransom is a burden of ownership (مؤنة الملك). Since the slave was bought with the mudaraba capital and profit appeared, the slave is owned three-quarters by the owner (his original capital plus half the profit) and one-quarter by the mudarib (his share of profit). Thus ransom is divided accordingly. The slave serves them proportionally: three days for owner, one for mudarib. If the slave's value were only one thousand (equal to capital, no profit), the mudarib would have no ownership, so only the owner decides. The passage also discusses procedural rules: for surrender (دفع) of the slave to pay the blood-money, both parties must be present because the mudarib has a right. For ransom (فداء), presence is not required except in certain cases. If the mudarib refuses both options and the value equals capital, the owner may surrender him. If one is absent and the other ransoms, he does so voluntarily and cannot recover from the absent partner. Finally, Qadikhan notes that the mudarib alone cannot decide on surrender or ransom because these are not part of the mudaraba contract.

Key Terms
فداء (fidā’): Ransom paid to free a slave from liability for manslaughter; the blood-money (diya) that the slave's owner pays to avoid surrendering the slave.
مضاربة (muḍārabah): A partnership where one party provides capital and the other provides labor, with profits shared as agreed; losses are borne solely by the capital provider.
دفع (daf‘): Surrendering the slave to the victim's family to satisfy the blood-money instead of paying ransom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a mudaraba where the mudarib buys a slave with capital and half-profit, what is the distribution of ransom if the slave commits manslaughter?
A) All ransom on the owner
B) Three-quarters on owner, one-quarter on mudarib
C) Half on each
D) All ransom on the mudarib

Key Takeaway
Ransom is a burden of ownership; when a mudaraba slave kills by mistake, the ransom is divided according to ownership shares, and surrender requires the presence of both owner and mudarib.

Division of Fidyah and Service When a Mudarabah Slave Commits Manslaughter
Ruling on division of fidyah and service when slave kills

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the division of fidyah and service when a mudarabah slave commits manslaughter, and identify the conditions for surrender and fidyah payment.

Core Idea
Fidyah and service shares follow ownership, which depends on profit distribution.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in mudarabah: if the mudarib buys a slave with capital and the slave kills someone by mistake, how are the ransom (fidyah) and the slave's service divided? The Hanafi ruling ties these shares directly to the ownership ratio of the slave, which in turn reflects the profit from the venture. We will also see the conditions under which the mudarib and owner must act jointly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Restate the basic facts: a mudarabah with capital of 1000 dirhams, profit share 50%, a slave bought for 2000 (exceeding capital), then the slave commits manslaughter. Note the values and parties: owner (rabb al-mal) and mudarib.
The slave's value exceeding capital generates profit, giving the mudarib ownership rights.
2
Calculate ownership shares
Determine how ownership of the slave is divided. The profit is 1000 (value 2000 – capital 1000). The mudarib gets half of that profit (500), so his share is 1/4 of the slave (500/2000). The owner gets the rest: 3/4.
This ratio drives the division of fidyah and service.
3
Apply the rule: fidyah and service follow ownership
State that fidyah (ransom to free the slave) is a burden of ownership, so it is divided in proportion: 3/4 on owner, 1/4 on mudarib. Similarly, the slave's service (to compensate for the tort?) is divided: owner gets 3 days, mudarib 1 day per week? The text says 3 days owner, 1 day mudarib.
This is the direct legal consequence of the ownership calculation.
4
Identify conditions for surrender and fidyah
Understand when both parties must act together. For surrendering the slave (daf'), both owner and mudarib must be present because the mudarib has a right in the slave. For fidyah, the presence of both is not required, except if the mudarib refuses both options and the slave's value equals the capital, then the owner may surrender alone due to obstinacy.
This parallels the rule for a pawned slave.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference: Qadi Khan's view
Qadi Khan holds that the mudarib cannot surrender or ransom the slave alone because these actions are not part of the mudarabah contract. The passage does not explicitly reject this, but the main ruling implies joint action for surrender.
This is a minority view; the relied-upon position is the one requiring joint presence for daf'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (معه ألف بالنصف فاشترى به عبداً قيمته ألفان فقتل رجلاً خطأ فثلاثة أرباع الفداء على المالك وربعه على المضارب والعبد يخدم المالك ثلاثة أيام والمضارب يوماً) لأن الفداء مؤنة الملك وقد كان الملك بينهما أرباعاً لأنه لما صار المال عيناً واحداً ظهر الربح وهو ألف بينهما وألف لرب المال، فإذا فدياه خرج العبد عن المضاربة لأن نصيب المضارب صار مضموناً عليه ونصيب رب المال صار له بقضاء القاضي بالفداء عليهما، وإذا خرج عنها بالدفع أو بالفداء يخدمهما على قدر ملكهما قيد بقوله قيمته ألفان لأنه لو كان قيمته ألفاً فتدبير الجناية إلى رب المال لأن الرقبة على ملكه لا ملك للمضارب فيها، فإن اختار رب الدفع واختار المضارب الفداء ذلك فله ذلك لأنه يستبقي بالفداء مال المضاربة وله ذلك لأن الربح يتوهم؛ كذا في الإيضاح . ثم اعلم أن العبد المشتري في المضاربة إذا جنى خطأ لا يدفع بها حتى يحضر المضارب ورب المال سواء كان الأرش مثل قيمة العبد أو أقل أو أكثر، وكذا إذا كانت قيمته ألفاً لا غير لا يدفع إلا بحضرتهما لأن المضارب له فيه حق ليس لرب المال أن يأخذه ويمنعه عن بيعه كالمرهون إذا جنى خطأ لا يدفع إلا بحضرة الراهن والمرتهن. والحاصل أنه يشترط حضرة رب المال والمضارب للدفع دون الفداء إلا إذا أبي المضارب الدفع والفداء وقيمته مثل رأس المال فلرب المال دفعه لتعنته، فإن كان أحدهما غائباً وقيمة العبد ألفا درهم ففداه الحاضر كان متطوعاً لأنه أدى دين غيره بغير أمره وهو غير مضطر فيه، فإنه لو أقام البينة على الشركة لا يطالب بحصة صاحبه لا بالدفع ولا بالفداء؛ كذا في النهاية. وذكر قاضيخان أن المضارب ليس له الدفع والفداء وحده لأنه ليس من أحكام المضاربة
He said: (He has a thousand [dirhams] in a mudarabah at half, and with it he bought a slave worth two thousand, and the slave killed a man by mistake: then three-fourths of the fidyah [ransom] is upon the owner and one-fourth upon the mudarib, and the slave serves the owner three days and the mudarib one day) because the fidyah is a burden of ownership, and the ownership was between them in fourths, because when the capital became one property, profit appeared: one thousand [profit] between them, and one thousand for the owner. Then, if they ransom him, the slave leaves the mudarabah because the mudarib's share becomes guaranteed upon him, and the owner's share becomes his by the judge's judgment of the fidyah upon them. And if he leaves by payment or by fidyah, he serves them according to their ownership. He restricted it by saying 'value two thousand' because if its value were one thousand, then the disposal of the tort is to the owner, because the corporeal property is in his ownership, the mudarib has no ownership in it. If the owner chooses payment and the mudarib chooses fidyah, that is permissible for him because by fidyah he preserves the mudarabah property, and that is permissible for him because profit can be hoped. In al-Idah. Then know that the slave bought in mudarabah, if he commits tort by mistake, he is not surrendered for it until the mudarib and owner are present, whether the compensation is equal to the slave's value or less or more. Likewise, if his value is only one thousand, he is not surrendered except in their presence because the mudarib has a right in him, and the owner may not take him and prevent his sale, like a pawn when it commits tort by mistake, it is not surrendered except in the presence of the pawner and the pledgee. The conclusion is that the presence of the owner and mudarib is required for surrender, but not for fidyah, except if the mudarib refuses both surrender and fidyah and the slave's value equals the capital, then the owner may surrender him due to his obstinacy. If one of them is absent and the slave's value is two thousand dirhams, then the one present who ransoms him is a volunteer because he paid the debt of another without his order and he is not compelled; even if he establishes evidence of partnership, he cannot claim the share of his partner, neither for surrender nor for fidyah. In al-Nihayah. And Qadi Khan mentioned that the mudarib does not have the right of surrender and fidyah alone because it is not from the rulings of mudarabah.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the Hanafi school on the scenario where a mudarib (agent in a commenda partnership) buys a slave using mudarabah capital, and that slave commits manslaughter. The key points: The fidyah (ransom to free the slave from liability) is divided according to ownership shares. Since the profit of 1000 emerged, ownership of the slave is 1/4 mudarib (his profit share) and 3/4 owner (capital + profit share). So fidyah is split accordingly. The slave then serves them in proportion to ownership (3 days owner, 1 day mudarib). If the slave's value is only 1000 (no profit), the mudarib has no ownership, so only the owner decides surrender or fidyah. The ruling also specifies that for surrender, both parties must be present because the mudarib has a right in the slave. For fidyah, it is not required unless the mudarib refuses and the slave's value equals the capital. If one is absent, the present one who pays fidyah does so voluntarily and cannot recover from the absent partner. Qadi Khan notes that the mudarib alone cannot surrender or ransom because these actions are not part of the mudarabah contract. This ruling is based on the principle that the mudarib's right in the slave is restricted to his profit share.

Key Terms
الفداء (al-fida'): The ransom payment to free a slave from liability for his tort. In this passage, it is divided between owner and mudarib according to ownership.
المضارب (al-mudarib): The agent or manager in a mudarabah partnership who invests the capital provided by the owner (rabb al-mal) and shares in the profit.
الدفع (al-daf'): Surrendering the slave to the victim's family to satisfy the tort claim, as opposed to paying fidyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 1 day out of 7
D) 2 days out of 7

Key Takeaway
Fidyah and service following ownership shares is the foundational principle for slave torts in mudarabah.

Resolving the Apparent Contradiction: Mudarabah and Murabahah Rulings
Author resolves alleged inconsistency between two rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two scenarios (mudarabah with no profit vs murabahah with profit) and state the correct ruling for each.

Core Idea
The two rulings are consistent — each applies to a distinct scenario of asset disposition.

Students of fiqh often notice that a single author seems to give contradictory rulings: one here and another in the chapter on murabahah. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses that confusion head-on, explaining that the rulings correspond to different factual settings. By carefully dissecting the scenarios — whether the mudarib sells to the owner at a surplus or the owner sells to the mudarib without cost — we see that both rulings are correct within their proper contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
Read the passage and note what readers claimed: that the author contradicted himself between the ruling in this chapter and the ruling in the chapter on murabahah.
Contradiction is only apparent, not real.
2
Locate the two distinct scenarios
Identify the first scenario: mudarib sells to the owner with no surplus of price over capital. Identify the second scenario (murabahah): mudarib sells to the owner at a profit, then the owner sells back to the mudarib.
The second scenario involves a profit that must be disclosed.
3
Apply the rule of murabahah
Murabahah requires full disclosure of cost and profit margin. In the second scenario, the mudarib must disclose that the garment was originally bought from the owner.
If disclosure is omitted, the sale is invalid.
4
Distinguish the legal basis
The first scenario has no surplus, so no murabahah issue. The second scenario has surplus (profit), so murabahah rules apply. The commentator refers to different sections in al-Muhit.
Both rulings are correct — they govern different facts.
5
Conclude: no contradiction
Recognize that when the scenarios are properly separated, the rulings are consistent. The confusion arose from mixing two distinct factual patterns.
Always check the factual setting before comparing rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وقد اشتبهت هذه المسألة على كثير من ذلك الكثير المؤلف نفسه حتى وفق بين كلاميه في باب المرابحة بغير ما هنا . وقد اشتبهت هذه المسألة على كثير حتى زعموا أنه وقع منه تناقض وليس كذلك بل ما ذكره هنا هو الوجه الأول في كلام أنه لا فضل في الثمن وقيمة المبيع على رأس المال وما ذكره في باب المرابحة هو القسم الثالث أو الرابع في كلام المحيط كما لا يخفى. ولهذا صوروا المسألة هناك بأن معه عشرة بالنصف فاشترى ثوباً بعشرة وباعه من رب المال بخمسة عشر قالوا يبيعه مرابحة باثني عشر ونصف، ولو ملكه رب المال بغير شيء فباعه من المضارب لا يبيعه مرابحة حتى يبين أنه اشتراه من رب المال؛ كذا في المحيط .
He said: (And this issue has been confused for many, even the author himself, until he reconciled between his two statements in the chapter of murabahah differently than here. And this issue has been confused for many until they claimed that a contradiction occurred from him, but it is not so; rather what he mentioned here is the first aspect in his statement that there is no surplus in the price and value of the sold item over the capital, and what he mentioned in the chapter of murabahah is the third or fourth section in the statement of al-Muhit, as is not hidden. And for this they posed the issue there: he has ten [dirhams] at half, so he bought a garment for ten and sold it to the owner for fifteen, they said he sells it at murabahah for twelve and a half, and if the owner owned it for nothing and sold it to the mudarib, he does not sell it at murabahah until he clarifies that he bought it from the owner. In al-Muhit.)
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the commentator (likely Ibn Nujaym) addressing a common misunderstanding. Some readers thought the author contradicted himself between the ruling in this chapter and that in the chapter on murabahah (cost-plus sale). The commentator clarifies that there is no contradiction: the ruling here deals with one scenario (where there is no surplus of price and value over capital), while the ruling in murabahah deals with a different scenario (third or fourth type in al-Muhit). He gives an example: in murabahah, if a mudarib has 10 dirhams at half profit, buys a garment for 10, and sells it to the owner for 15, he sells it at murabahah for 12.5 (because the owner is entitled to half the profit). But if the owner owned the garment without any cost, he cannot sell it at murabahah to the mudarib without disclosing that he bought it from the owner. So the rulings are consistent within their proper contexts.

Key Terms
المرابحة (al-murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the cost and profit margin. In this context, it involves a mudarabah scenario where the sold item is bought from the owner.
المضاربة (al-mudarabah): A partnership where one party provides capital (rab al-mal) and the other provides labor (mudarib), with profits shared as agreed.
رب المال (rab al-mal): The owner of the capital in a mudarabah contract.
المحيط (al-Muhit): A Hanafi legal reference work (al-Muhit al-Burhani) used as authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The third or fourth section in al-Muhit (with surplus)
C) The author's later correction
D) Ijma of the Hanafi school

Key Takeaway
The rulings are consistent — each applies to a distinct scenario of asset disposition.

Dispute over Capital Amount in Mudarabah
Rules for capital amount dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the mudarib's word is accepted on the amount of capital received and determine when evidence shifts the preference to the owner.

Core Idea
The receiver's word on quantity is accepted, even if he is a guarantor.

When the mudarib and the owner disagree on how much capital was given, whose statement is accepted? This lesson explains the Hanafi default rule: the mudarib, as the receiver of the property, gets the benefit of the doubt. However, if both parties produce evidence, the owner's evidence regarding excess capital is preferred. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for resolving mudarabah disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of dispute
Determine whether the disagreement is over the amount of capital, the amount of profit, or the quality of the received property. Each type has a different default rule.
In this lesson we focus on capital amount.
2
Apply the default rule for capital disputes
Since the mudarib is the one who physically received the capital, his word on its quantity is accepted, provided he takes an oath (if no evidence). This even applies if he is a guarantor (ḍamīn) for his part.
Analogy to a case where the receiver denies receiving anything at all.
3
Consider when evidence is presented
If only one party brings evidence, that evidence is accepted. If both bring evidence, the owner's evidence on the capital amount is preferred because he is the owner and his claim of excess is backed by proof.
For profit disputes, the opposite applies: the mudarib's evidence on profit excess is preferred.
4
Distinguish from disputes over profit or quality
If the dispute is about the amount of profit, the owner's word is accepted. If the dispute is about the quality of the received property, the owner's word is also accepted (as will come later).
The text explicitly restricts the capital rule to quantity disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (معه ألفان فقال دفعت إلي ألفاً وربحت ألفاً وقال المالك دفعت ألفين فالقول للمضارب) لأنهما اختلفا في المقبوض والقول في مقداره للقابض ولو ضميناً اعتباراً بما لو أنكره أصلاً فإن القول له، ولو كان الاختلاف ذلك في قدر الربح فالقول لرب المال في مقدار الربح فقط وأيهما أقام البينة تقبل بينته وإن أقاما فتقبل بينة رب المال في دعواه الزيادة في رأس المال والمضارب في دعواه والزيادة في الربح قيد الاختلاف بكونه في المقدار لأن الاختلاف إذا وقع في صفة المقبوض فالقول قول رب المال كما سيأتي قوله : (معه ألف فقال هو مضاربة بالنصف وقد ربح ألفاً وقال المالك هو بضاعة فالقول للمالك) لأن المضارب يدعي عليه تقويم عمله أو شرطاً من جهته أو يدعي الشركة وهو ينكر، والتقييد بالمضاربة والبضاعة ليس احترازاً مطلقاً بل لو قال المضارب هي قرض وقال رب بضاعة أو وديعة أو مضاربة فالقول لرب المال والبينة بينة المضارب لأن المضارب يدعي عليه ينكر، بل احتراز عما لو ادعى رب المال القرض والمضارب المضاربة كان القول للمضارب لأن رب المال يدعي عليه ضماناً وهو ينكر وأيهما أقامها قبلت، وإن أقاماها فبينة رب المال أولى. قيد الاختلاف بكونه في الصفة لأنه لو كان في النوع بأن ادعى رب المضاربة في نوع وقال المضارب ما سميت لي تجارة بعينها فالقول للمضارب مع يمينه لأن الأصل فيه العموم والإطلاق والتخصيص يعارض وتقبل بينة من أقامها فإن أقاماها فإن وقتنا وقتاً قبل صاحبها يقضى بالمتأخرة، وإن لم يوقتا وقتاً على السواء أو وقتت أحدهما دون الأخرى قضى ببينة رب المال؛ كذا في الذخيرة. ولو ادعى كل واحد منهما نوعاً فالقول لرب المال لأنهما اتفقا على التخصيص والإذن يستفاد من جهته والبيئة بينة المضارب لحاجته إلى الضمان وعدم حاجة الآخر إلى البينة ولو وقتت البينتان وقتاً فصاحب الوقت الأخير أولى لأن آخر الشرطين ينقض الأول؛ كذا في الهداية. وإن كان رب المال يدعي العموم فالقول قوله قياساً واستحساناً؛ كذا في الذخيرة والله تعالى أعلم.
He said: (He has two thousand, so he says: You gave me one thousand and I earned one thousand profit, and the owner says: I gave two thousand. The word is the mudarib's) because they dispute over the received amount, and the word on its quantity is of the receiver, even if he is a guarantor, by analogy with if he denied entirely, then the word is his. If the dispute is over the amount of profit, then the word is the owner's in the amount of profit only. Whichever of them produces evidence, his evidence is accepted. If both produce evidence, then the evidence of the owner regarding his claim of excess in capital is accepted, and the mudarib's evidence regarding his claim of excess in profit. He restricted the dispute to being about quantity, because if the dispute is about the quality of the received property, then the word is the owner's, as will come. He said: (He has one thousand, so he says it is mudarabah at half and I have earned one thousand, and the owner says it is a bida'ah [deposit], then the word is the owner's) because the mudarib claims compensation for his work or a stipulation from him or claims partnership while he denies. The restriction to mudarabah and bida'ah is not absolute; rather if the mudarib says it is a loan and the owner says bida'ah, wadi'ah or mudarabah, then the word is the owner's, and the evidence is the mudarib's because the mudarib claims something against him which he denies. Rather it is an exception from the case where the owner claims a loan and the mudarib claims mudarabah: the word is the mudarib's because the owner claims a guarantee against him and he denies. Whichever of them produces evidence, it is accepted; if both produce it, the owner's evidence is preferable. He restricted the dispute to being about quality because if it is about type—such as the owner claims mudarabah in a specific type and the mudarib says you did not name a specific trade—then the word is the mudarib's with his oath because the default is generality and absolutism, and specification conflicts. The evidence of whoever produces it is accepted. If both produce evidence and they specify a time, the later time is given judgment; if they do not specify a time both equally, or one specifies and the other does not, the owner's evidence is given judgment. In al-Dhakhirah. If each of them claims a type, the word is the owner's because they agreed on specification and authorization is derived from him, and the evidence is the mudarib's due to his need for guarantee and the other's lack of need. If both pieces of evidence specify a time, the later time is given priority because the later condition abrogates the first. In al-Hidayah. And if the owner claims generality, the word is his by analogy and istihsan. In al-Dhakhirah. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage sets out Hanafi rules for resolving disputes in a mudarabah contract. It covers three types of disagreement: (1) Dispute over the amount of capital given: the mudarib's word is accepted because he is the receiver of the property, even if he is a guarantor for his part. But if the dispute is about profit amount, the owner's word is taken. If both bring evidence, the owner's evidence on capital and mudarib's on profit is preferred. (2) Dispute over the nature of the contract: if the mudarib claims mudarabah and the owner claims bida'ah (a deposit without profit share), the owner's word is accepted because the mudarib is claiming something additional (profit share). However, if the mudarib claims loan and owner claims bida'ah, the owner's word still stands. But if owner claims loan and mudarib claims mudarabah, the mudarib's word is accepted because the owner is claiming a guarantee against him. (3) Dispute over whether the mudarabah was restricted to a specific trade: if the owner claims a specific trade and the mudarib denies, the mudarib's word with oath is accepted because the default is unrestricted authorization. If both bring evidence with timestamps, later evidence prevails; if times are equal or one is unspecified, owner's evidence is preferred. If both claim specific but different types, the owner's word is accepted. If the owner claims the mudarabah was general, his word is accepted by analogy and istihsan. These rulings demonstrate the Hanafi emphasis on the owner's ownership of capital and the mudarib's trustee role.

Key Terms
القول قول القابض (al-qawl qawl al-qabid): The legal maxim that the word of the person who received property is accepted regarding its quantity in a dispute with the giver.
البضاعة (al-bida'ah): A deposit or arrangement where the agent trades without profit share; it is like a bailment for trading.
اليمين (al-yamin): Oath taken by the party whose statement is accepted when there is no evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a mudarabah disagreement over capital, if the owner brings evidence that he gave $10,000 and the mudarib brings no evidence, what is the ruling?
A) The mudarib's word is accepted.
B) The owner's evidence is accepted.
C) Both statements are rejected.
D) The case is dismissed.

Key Takeaway
In disputes over capital amount, the mudarib's word is the default; but evidence from the owner overrides.

Mudarabah — Profit-Sharing

Dispute over Contract Nature: Mudarabah vs. Bida'ah
Rules for contract type dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whose word is accepted when the mudarib and owner disagree on the type of contract (mudarabah, bida'ah, loan, etc.) and apply the evidence rules.

Core Idea
The owner's word on the contract type is accepted unless it imposes a guarantee on the mudarib.

When the parties dispute whether the arrangement was a mudarabah (profit-sharing) or a bida'ah (deposit without profit), who prevails? The Hanafi rule is that the owner's word is generally accepted because he denies the additional obligations claimed by the mudarib. However, if the owner claims a loan (which imposes guarantee on the mudarib), the mudarib's word is accepted. This lesson unpacks these nuanced rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing claims
List what each party is claiming. For example, mudarib claims mudarabah (profit share), owner claims bida'ah (no profit).
2
Apply the default: owner's word
When the mudarib claims something extra (profit share, compensation), the owner's denial is accepted because the mudarib is alleging a right against the owner.
The text: 'because the mudarib claims compensation for his work or a stipulation from him or claims partnership while he denies.'
3
Recognize the exception: loan claim
If the owner claims a loan (qarḍ) and the mudarib claims mudarabah, the mudarib's word is accepted because the owner is imposing a guarantee liability on the mudarib.
Loan makes the mudarib a guarantor, which he denies.
4
Evaluate evidence
Whichever party brings evidence, it is accepted. If both bring evidence, the owner's evidence is preferred (except in the loan exception?).
The text says: 'And whichever of them produces evidence, it is accepted; if both produce it, the owner's evidence is preferable.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Dispute over Trade Restrictions in Mudarabah
Rules for trade restriction disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for disputes over whether the mudarabah was restricted to a specific trade and analyze evidence with timestamps.

Core Idea
The default mudarabah is unrestricted; the mudarib's word is accepted on generality but evidence with later dates overrides.

When the owner claims the mudarabah was for a specific trade but the mudarib claims no restriction, or they both claim different specific trades, how is the dispute resolved? This lesson covers these scenarios and the complex evidence rules involving timestamps. Understanding these rules is essential for partners to define the scope of authorization.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of dispute
Is the dispute about generality vs. specificity (owner claims specific, mudarib denies) or about two different specifics?
2
Apply the default for generality vs. specificity
If the owner claims a specific trade and the mudarib denies, the mudarib's word with oath is accepted because the default is generality (al-aṣl al-ʿumūm wa al-iṭlāq).
Specification is a burden on the owner.
3
Apply the default for two specifics
If both claim different specific trades, the owner's word is accepted because they agree there was a specification and authorization comes from the owner.
The mudarib's evidence is preferred if his need for guarantee is stronger? Actually text says: evidence is mudarib's.
4
Evaluate evidence with time
If both bring evidence, the later-dated evidence prevails (last condition abrogates earlier). If times equal or one unspecified, owner's evidence wins.
From al-Hidayah and al-Dhakhirah.
5
Consider the owner's claim of generality
If the owner claims the mudarabah was general, his word is accepted by qiyas and istihsan.
This is a separate scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (معه ألفان فقال دفعت إلي ألفاً وربحت ألفاً وقال المالك دفعت ألفين فالقول للمضارب) لأنهما اختلفا في المقبوض والقول في مقداره للقابض ولو ضميناً اعتباراً بما لو أنكره أصلاً فإن القول له، ولو كان الاختلاف ذلك في قدر الربح فالقول لرب المال في مقدار الربح فقط وأيهما أقام البينة تقبل بينته وإن أقاما فتقبل بينة رب المال في دعواه الزيادة في رأس المال والمضارب في دعواه والزيادة في الربح قيد الاختلاف بكونه في المقدار لأن الاختلاف إذا وقع في صفة المقبوض فالقول قول رب المال كما سيأتي قوله : (معه ألف فقال هو مضاربة بالنصف وقد ربح ألفاً وقال المالك هو بضاعة فالقول للمالك) لأن المضارب يدعي عليه تقويم عمله أو شرطاً من جهته أو يدعي الشركة وهو ينكر، والتقييد بالمضاربة والبضاعة ليس احترازاً مطلقاً بل لو قال المضارب هي قرض وقال رب بضاعة أو وديعة أو مضاربة فالقول لرب المال والبينة بينة المضارب لأن المضارب يدعي عليه ينكر، بل احتراز عما لو ادعى رب المال القرض والمضارب المضاربة كان القول للمضارب لأن رب المال يدعي عليه ضماناً وهو ينكر وأيهما أقامها قبلت، وإن أقاماها فبينة رب المال أولى. قيد الاختلاف بكونه في الصفة لأنه لو كان في النوع بأن ادعى رب المضاربة في نوع وقال المضارب ما سميت لي تجارة بعينها فالقول للمضارب مع يمينه لأن الأصل فيه العموم والإطلاق والتخصيص يعارض وتقبل بينة من أقامها فإن أقاماها فإن وقتنا وقتاً قبل صاحبها يقضى بالمتأخرة، وإن لم يوقتا وقتاً على السواء أو وقتت أحدهما دون الأخرى قضى ببينة رب المال؛ كذا في الذخيرة. ولو ادعى كل واحد منهما نوعاً فالقول لرب المال لأنهما اتفقا على التخصيص والإذن يستفاد من جهته والبيئة بينة المضارب لحاجته إلى الضمان وعدم حاجة الآخر إلى البينة ولو وقتت البينتان وقتاً فصاحب الوقت الأخير أولى لأن آخر الشرطين ينقض الأول؛ كذا في الهداية. وإن كان رب المال يدعي العموم فالقول قوله قياساً واستحساناً؛ كذا في الذخيرة والله تعالى أعلم.

However, if the mudarib claims loan and owner claims bida'ah, the owner's word still stands. But if owner claims loan and mudarib claims mudarabah, the mudarib's word is accepted because the owner is claiming a guarantee against him. (3) Dispute over whether the mudarabah was restricted to a specific trade: if the owner claims a specific trade and the mudarib denies, the mudarib's word with oath is accepted because the default is unrestricted authorization. If both bring evidence with timestamps, later evidence prevails; if times are equal or one is unspecified, owner's evidence is preferred. If both claim specific but different types, the owner's word is accepted. If the owner claims the mudarabah was general, his word is accepted by analogy and istihsan. These rulings demonstrate the Hanafi emphasis on the owner's ownership of capital and the mudarib's trustee role.

Key Terms
القول قول القابض (al-qawl qawl al-qabid): The legal maxim that the word of the person who received property is accepted regarding its quantity in a dispute with the giver.
البضاعة (al-bida'ah): A deposit or arrangement where the agent trades without profit share; it is like a bailment for trading.
اليمين (al-yamin): Oath taken by the party whose statement is accepted when there is no evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If both the owner and mudarib claim different specific trades, whose word is accepted on the type?
A) The mudarib.
B) The owner.
C) The one with earlier evidence.
D) Neither; the court decides.

Key Takeaway
Trade restriction disputes: mudarib's word if owner claims specific and mudarib denies; owner's word if both specify; later evidence overrides earlier.
